-53-238_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=NcmQaF_H5To:i93BDduHyhE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn52@2020_6/2020/11/17/05-38-48-838_10560a8005137654.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/NcmQaF_H5To":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn75@2020_2/2020/11/17/05-38-49-064_b1b844c7b3ca61ea.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605591522167},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"Moderna and Pfizer's coronavirus vaccines are more than 90% effective. Here's how that compares to shots for the flu, measles, and more.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-compares-other-vaccines-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa94758f7d1cb0019e3a758?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1229305135\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A healthcare worker injects a patient with the Pfizer and BioNTech coronavirus vaccine during the phase 3 trial in Turkey in October.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dogukan Keskinkilic/Anadolu Agency via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Moderna announced Monday that its coronavirus vaccine candidate was found to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">94.5% effective in preventing COVID-19 in clinical trials</a>.</li>\n<li>Pfizer announced last week that its coronavirus vaccine candidate was found to be more than <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">90%</a> effective.</li>\n<li>The chart below shows how those vaccine candidates' efficacy compares to the effectiveness of vaccines for chickenpox, flu, measles, and polio.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Moderna, a Massachusetts-based biotech firm, announced Monday that trial results so far suggest its vaccine is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">94.5% effective</a> in preventing COVID-19. It's the second company to report positive findings from the final stage of clinical trials: Last week, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">Pfizer</a> and BioNTech <a href=\"https://investors.pfizer.com/investor-news/press-release-details/2020/Pfizer-and-BioNTech-Announce-Vaccine-Candidate-Against-COVID-19-Achieved-Success-in-First-Interim-Analysis-from-Phase-3-Study/default.aspx\">reported</a> that their vaccine was found to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-compares-other-vaccines-2020-11\">more than 90% effective</a>.</p><p>\"Now we have two vaccines that are really quite effective. I think this is a really strong step forward to where we want to be about getting control of this outbreak,\" Anthony Fauci, director of the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases, <a href=\"https://on.today.com/3kyGckI\">told NBC's Today on Monday</a>.</p><p>The Food and Drug Administration has said any coronavirus shot must be at least 50% effective to get authorization. Most experts had hoped for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-ultimate-guide-to-interpreting-phase-3-coronavirus-vaccine-results-2020-9\">70% efficacy or higher</a>.</p><p>Not all vaccines are equally effective. Some, like the seasonal flu vaccine, <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/flu/vaccines-work/effectiveness-studies.htm\">hover below 60%</a>. Others, like the polio vaccine, are <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/vaccines/vpd/polio/hcp/effectiveness-duration-protection.html\">almost 100% effective</a>.</p><p>Here's how Moderna and Pfizer's coronavirus vaccine candidates compare to four existing vaccines.</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe title=\"How Moderna and Pfizer coronavirus vaccines compare to vaccines for other viruses\" aria-label=\"chart\" id=\"datawrapper-chart-1WDMo\" src=\"https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/1WDMo/3/\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"width: 0; min-width: 100% ; border: none;\" height=\"511\"></iframe><script type=\"text/javascript\">!function(){\"use strict\";window.addEventListener(\"message\",(function(a){if(void 0!==a.data[\"datawrapper-height\"])for(var e in a.data[\"datawrapper-height\"]){var t=document.getElementById(\"datawrapper-chart-\"+e)||document.querySelector(\"iframe[src*='\"+e+\"']\");t&&(t.style.height=a.data[\"datawrapper-height\"][e]+\"px\")}}))}();</script></div><p>&#160;</p><h2>How experts measure vaccine effectiveness&#160;</h2><p>The polio vaccine has been distributed for 65 years — plenty of time for scientists to build a thorough understanding of its effectiveness. That's a measure of how much it reduces the incidence of cases among people who get vaccinated relative to those who do not.&#160;</p><p>The greater that reduction, the higher the <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/csels/dsepd/ss1978/lesson3/section6.html\">vaccine's effectiveness</a>.</p><p>Because Moderna and Pfizer's coronavirus vaccine candidates have only been tested in clinical trials however, their reports center on a measure known as vaccine efficacy. It's a calculation of how effective the vaccine could be given ideal circumstances in which everyone is given the shot.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb1d6641c741f0019ac9e48?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Moderna vaccine\" height=\"683\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A nurse prepares a coronavirus vaccine shot developed by the National Institutes of Health and Moderna Inc., July 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hans Pennink/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Moderna's announcement was based on 95 cases of COVID-19 observed among the 30,000 participants in its phase 3 clinical trial. Among that larger group, some people were given the company's experimental vaccine while others just got a placebo injection.</p><p>Out of those 95 cases, 90 of them were people who'd gotten a placebo shot. Just five people who got COVID-19 had received Moderna's vaccine. The results showed that the vaccine not only prevented mild COVID-19 among participants, it also also appeared to prevent serious illness too. Researchers found 11 cases of severe COVID-19 among the placebo group and zero among those who got the vaccine.</p><p>Pfizer's vaccine, meanwhile was also found to prevent mild illness, but the company didn't reveal whether its shot prevented serious coronavirus infections, too.</p><p>It's also still unclear whether either vaccine <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/unanswered-questions-about-pfizers-coronavirus-vaccine-what-we-dont-know-2020-11\">prevents asymptomatic coronavirus infections</a>, because trial participants were only tested for COVID-19 if they experienced symptoms.</p><h2>A 2-dose regimen</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f552d7fe6ff30001d4e7564?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Moderna coronavirus vaccine trial participant\" height=\"3693\" width=\"4924\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nurse Kath Olmstead, right, gives volunteer Melissa Harting an injection of Moderna&#39;s experimental coronavirus vaccine, July 27, 2020, in Binghamton, New York.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hans Pennink/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Both Moderna and Pfizer's vaccines require two shots. Moderna's two doses are administered <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-requires-2-shots-month-apart-2020-11\">a month apart</a>, while <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-2-shots-2020-11\">Pfizer's</a> are given three weeks apart.&#160;</p><p>Many other vaccines — including the one that protects against measles — also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-compares-other-vaccines-2020-11\">require back-to-back doses to be most effective</a>. Two doses of the MMR (measles, mumps, rubella) vaccine are 97% effective at protecting someone from measles, whereas a single dose is 93% effective.</p><p>Other coronavirus vaccine candidates still in trials may require two shots as well, including AstraZeneca's; the company's phase 3 trial is testing <a href=\"https://www.nih.gov/news-events/news-releases/phase-3-clinical-testing-us-astrazeneca-covid-19-vaccine-candidate-begins\">two shots given four weeks apart</a>. Johnson &#38; Johnson, meanwhile, is testing both <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/09/23/health/johnson--johnson-coronavirus-vaccine-trial-begins/index.html\">a single-dose</a> and a two-dose vaccine in simultaneous <a href=\"https://www.jnj.com/johnson-johnson-initiates-second-global-phase-3-clinical-trial-of-its-janssen-covid-19-vaccine-candidate\">phase 3 trials</a>.</p><h2>Why the coronavirus vaccine will likely be more effective than a flu shot</h2><p>Viruses mutate over time: As they replicate, minute errors are introduced into the virus' genetic code, and those can then spread through a virus' population. While most mutations are inconsequential, occasionally one can appear that undermines people's immunity. But the new coronavirus mutates slowly, which means a vaccine would most likely be effective long-term against any existing viral strains.</p><p>The flu, by contrast, mutates quickly, which is why a new vaccine is needed each year.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f89e783d260780019341ea0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"how does the flu shot work\" height=\"1414\" width=\"2121\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A doctor gives a flu shot.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Marko Geber/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Both Pfizer and Moderna <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">plan to request emergency approval</a> for their coronavirus vaccines from the FDA in the new few weeks.</p><p>But neither company's clinical trial is complete yet, and neither <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-pfizer-vaccine-will-not-save-the-holidays-experts-2020-11\">has published their data</a> or submitted findings to a peer-reviewed medical journal or regulators. So <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-to-know-about-first-effective-coronavirus-vaccine-pfizer-2020-11\">many questions remain</a>.</p><p>Still, according to Moderna CEO Stephane Bancel, the company plans to produce <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-ceo-coronavirus-vaccine-timeline-when-will-i-get-a-shot-2020-11\">100 million doses</a> — enough to vaccinate 50 million people — by the end of March 2021. Pfizer has said the bulk of its doses — up to 1.3 billion — will be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/timeline-of-when-pfizer-covid-19-vaccine-could-be-available-2020-11\">ready sometime in 2021</a> as well.</p><p><em>Andrew Dunn contributed reporting to this story.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a At online startups like <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=74508&urllink=madeincookware.com%2F%3Futm_source%3Dshareasale%26utm_campaign%3D1088116%26utm_medium%3Daffiliate%26utm_term%3D999%26sscid%3Db1k4_hwfua3Db1k4_hwfua\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">Made In</a> and <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=81082&urllink=cookpotluck.com%2F%3Futm_source%3D1088116%26utm_medium%3Daffiliate%26sscid%3Db1k4_hwfuq3Db1k4_hwfuq\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\">Potluck</a>, you can find durable and versatile pots and pans at more affordable prices than equipment from big-name brands like All-Clad or Calphalon.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Ftchen.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Sardel</a> is the newest online cookware company to enter the fray and impress us. Founded by three brothers who wanted to cut down the clutter of poorly made kitchenware, they created the cookware collection they've always wanted for themselves — inexpensive, unintimidating, and made with high-quality materials.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Ffull-sets%2Ffull-set\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dea8942fd9db201b60c15e5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sardel cookware 2\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sardel full set, on sale for $520\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sardel/Instagram</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>The six pieces are made in Italy and all have a five-ply construction of stainless steel at the top and bottom layers, and an aluminum core, which provides them with great heat distribution and retention capabilities, as well as lifelong durability. If you're unsatisfied with the quality, you have 30 days to return for free; if there are defects in manufacturing under normal use, you can take the brand up on the limited lifetime warranty.&#160;</p><p>The designs are as classic as cookware gets, and that's the point. There are no gimmicks, merely the promise that the pieces will perform for all kinds of cooking tasks and won't cost a fortune. Each pan is priced between $80 and $145, but there are also <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Ffull-sets%2Ffull-set\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow\">discounted bundled options</a> if you're thinking of overhauling your existing cookware set.&#160;</p><p>We tried a number of Sardel's pans in our own kitchens, where they've become new favorites. Read on to find out how they performed.&#160;</p><h2><strong>The pans we tested:&#160;</strong></h2><ol><li><a (10-inch)</a>, $80, tested by Sally Kaplan, senior editor</li><li><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fproducts%2F10-non-stick10-non-stick\" Pan (4-quart)</a>, $130, tested by Connie Chen, senior reporter&#160;</li></ol><h2>Testing heat distribution and retention:</h2><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2F12-skillet2F12-skillet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dea90e8fd9db2112416c042?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sardel cookware 6\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sardel 12-inch Skillet, $95\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sardel</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>\"After years of working in professional catering kitchens, I've come to appreciate the importance of heat distribution — particularly when you're working with a large pot or pan over a small flame. I used the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2F10-skillet2F10-skillet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">10-inch skillet</a> on a few differently sized burners just to see how well the pan held its heat, and from my tests, I came away with perfectly crispy and evenly cooked latkes, vegan Beyond Sausages, and sauteed broccolini — even when cooking on the tiniest of burners. The <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Fsaucepans%2Fsaucepan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">two-quart saucepan</a> is just as excellent.\" <strong>—Sally&#160;</strong></p><p>\"I've never made more evenly cooked scrambled eggs in my life. The <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fproducts%2F10-non-stick10-non-stick\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Nonstick Skillet</a>'s heat distribution is excellent; the edges of the pan cook at the same rate as the middle. It's a marvel of engineering\". <strong>—Ellen</strong></p><p>\"Does the pan cook food quickly and efficiently? Does it retain the heat necessary to do so? These are simple tests that immediately distinguish the good from the bad, and Sardel passed with flying colors. Cooking with the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2F12-skillet2F12-skillet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Skillet</a> feels effortless while cooking with the large <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Fsaute-pan%2Fsaute-pan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Sauté Pan</a> is also surprisingly easy due to the effective combination of stainless steel and aluminum.\" <strong>—Connie&#160;</strong></p><div id=\"ProductCard_5dea920afd9db20a3c665472\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5dea920afd9db20a3c665472&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><h2>Testing construction and feel:&#160;</h2><p>\"Both the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2F10-skillet2F10-skillet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">10-inch skillet</a> and the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Fsaucepans%2Fsaucepan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">two-quart saucepan</a> feature Sardel's signature ergonomic handles, and for this, I am eternally grateful. I cook rather aggressively by shaking my pots and pans to flip or stir things, which is hard to do when you have a poorly shaped handle digging into your palm. The rounded handles on Sardel's cookware make it comfortable and easy for me to cook deftly, especially when the food I'm cooking is heavy.\"<strong>&#160;—Sally&#160;</strong></p><p>\"The <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fproducts%2F10-non-stick10-non-stick\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Nonstick Skillet</a> feels substantial in the hand, but not too heavy; the stainless steel handle is heat-resistant, too, so there's no fear of grabbing it with my bare hands.\" <strong>—Ellen&#160;</strong></p><p>\"Handles aren't the primary reason to buy cookware, but when they're good, you notice. The handles on my <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2F12-skillet2F12-skillet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Skillet</a> and <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Fsaute-pan%2Fsaute-pan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Sauté Pan</a> felt very durable and sturdy. And since they're actually hollow, they were never too hot to hold with my bare hands.\" <strong>—Connie&#160;</strong></p><div id=\"ProductCard_5dea9b87fd9db21c0b67a107\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5dea9b87fd9db21c0b67a107&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><h2>Testing versatility:&#160;&#160;</h2><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Fsaute-pan%2Fsaute-pan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dea8b2afd9db2037a4b79aa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sardel cookware\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Using the Sardel 4-quart Sauté Pan to make a pasta dish\n<p class=\"copyright\">Connie Chen/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>\"I mean, you can't really beat a stainless steel <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2F10-skillet2F10-skillet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">10-inch skillet</a> and a <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Fsaucepans%2Fsaucepan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">two-quart saucepan</a> as far as versatility goes — they're both sizes you'll use often. The skillet is just the right size for sauteeing veggies for two, searing two servings of protein, and pan-frying four latkes at a time. The two-quart saucepan is great for cooking and heating sauces, making small servings of soup (who really eats the same leftovers for four days straight anyway?), or even cooking single to double servings of smaller pasta shapes like bowties.\" <strong>—Sally&#160;</strong></p><p>\"Everyone needs a 10-inch <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fproducts%2F10-non-stick10-non-stick\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Nonstick Skillet</a> in their kitchen arsenal for cooking eggs and pancakes, and Sardel's $90 one is worth every penny. It's a perfect size for sauteing single servings of veggies, too\".<strong> —Ellen&#160;</strong></p><p>\"My easy fallback meal when I don't want to exert a lot of effort but still want a nourishing dinner is usually some type of pasta dish, and thanks to Sardel's large <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2Fsaute-pan%2Fsaute-pan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Sauté Pan</a>, I can make an entire salmon and spinach alfredo in one pan. It pan-roasts and sautés as well as a skillet, but because of the 2.5-inch straight walls, I can also stir large batches of sauce and pasta in it right afterward. I use the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fcollections%2Ffrontpage%2Fproducts%2F12-skillet2F12-skillet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Skillet</a> for less intensive meals, and it's always a reliable choice for cooking practically any meat or vegetable I want.\" <strong>—Connie&#160;</strong></p><div id=\"ProductCard_5dea8c0bfd9db20ddc787582\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5dea8c0bfd9db20ddc787582&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><h2>Testing ease of use and care:</h2><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fproducts%2F10-non-stick10-non-stick\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dee57eafd9db239f955aeb7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sardel cookware 9\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Using the Sardel Nonstick 10-inch Skillet to make scrambled eggs\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ellen Hoffman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>\"I had a tough time cleaning my skillet after frying a ton of latkes in it, but I also used several other large stainless steel pans to fry them and each one had the exact same issue of oil caking on and sticking. So I don't think it was the pan that created the issue, because it's been easy to clean every other time besides this one.\" <strong>—Sally&#160;</strong></p><p>\"Egg remnants <em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">glide</em> off this pan with little more than a stream of hot water and the single swipe of a soapy sponge. Although Sardel says the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fproducts%2F10-non-stick10-non-stick\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Nonstick Skillet</a> is very durable and dishwasher safe, I always hand-wash it and only use wooden or silicone utensils when cooking to prevent damaging the non-stick surface.\" <strong>—Ellen&#160;</strong></p><p>\"I've noticed that Sardel's pans are easier to clean than other pans I've tried, and I like that there aren't any special restrictions on how to clean and use them. The site also offers <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=88585&urllink=sardelkitchen.com%2Fblogs%2Ftips%2Fhow-to-care-for-your-stainless-steel-cookwareeel-cookware\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored\">care tips</a> to get the most out of your cookware. While they may seem basic, they're excellent foundational tips for anyone starting out in the kitchen and helpful reminders for seasoned home cooks.\" <strong>—Connie&#160;</strong></p><div (Connie Chen)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5dea7f7ffd9db27deb5bfb58?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn11@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-48-579_4969ebcc051ad4f9.webp","https://i.insider.com/5dea8942fd9db201b60c15e5?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn49@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-38-46-666_0be8d9b8dbd61015.webp","https://i.insider.com/5dea90e8fd9db2112416c042?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn3@2020_6/2020/11/17/05-38-42-615_5c1e75462147f77c.webp","https://i.insider.com/5dea8b2afd9db2037a4b79aa?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn88@2020_2/2020/11/17/05-38-59-661_3ebc7c5c28da73e0.webp","https://i.insider.com/5dee57eafd9db239f955aeb7?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn55@2020_2/2020/11/17/05-39-02-402_bb6f1158f57b6417.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn44@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-39-00-474_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=mWDThQ10rdg:_jWYuKSx5iE:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn55@2020_2/2020/11/17/05-38-46-781_45a1acae179f85d7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=mWDThQ10rdg:_jWYuKSx5iE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn87@2020_6/2020/11/17/05-38-50-509_8eef1aca5807e1ce.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-53-238_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=mWDThQ10rdg:_jWYuKSx5iE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn11@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-38-47-711_ef0b37a89eec580d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/mWDThQ10rdg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn47@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-51-334_b8d7a649a05ee2b7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605591522182},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"Airbnb just filed for its IPO, and it named the ongoing pandemic and steadily declining revenue growth in a lengthy list of risk factors","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ipo-risk-factors-pandemic-declining-revenue-not-profitable-2020-11","description":"<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2e92a1c741f0019aca1c3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky, Airbnb CEO\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption>\n   Airbnb CEO Brian Chesky. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Dia Dipasupil/Getty Images</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li><strong>Home-sharing company Airbnb filed for its initial public offering on Monday afternoon.</strong></li> \n <li><strong>The \"Risk Factors\" section of the document highlights how hard the coronavirus pandemic has been on the company, and how severely in debt it was even before 2020.</strong></li> \n <li><strong>Everything from the impacts of COVID-19 to the company's struggles with lawmakers is highlighted and detailed by Airbnb as potential risks to its business. We break down the full list below.</strong></li> \n <li><strong><a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories.</a></strong></li> \n</ul>\n<p>After over 12 years in business, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-files-s1-public-ipo-paperwork-revenue-losses-covid-19-2020-11\">Airbnb is finally going public</a>.</p>\n<p>The home-rental company filed a form S-1 for its IPO with the Securities and Exchange Commission on Monday afternoon. That included disclosing a trove of information that was previously unknown. For starters: Airbnb is over $2 billion in debt.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ceo-brian-chesky-pandemic-challenges-resiliency-ipo-interview-2020-9\">Airbnb's Brian Chesky says what it was like to watch his company's revenue plunge 80% in eight weeks and how he decided to go public anyway in exclusive interview</a></em></p>\n<p>But that's far from all the filing document has to offer — a section labeled \"Risk Factors\" details the major issues Airbnb believes it could face. We break down the most important of those potential issues below:</p> \n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n  1. The coronavirus pandemic has hurt Airbnb, and could continue to hurt the company. \n <figure> \n  <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f46d7becd2fec00296a46c4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbnb Open Homes  Photo\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\"> \n   <figcaption>\n    A member of the Airbnb Open Homes program. \n    <p class=\"copyright\">Airbnb</p> \n   </figcaption> </img>\n </figure> \n <p>With millions of people around the world staying home throughout 2020 as the coronavirus pandemic spread from country to country, Airbnb rentals dropped off a cliff.</p>\n <p>The company took drastic measures to stem the bleeding: It cut its full-time workforce by a quarter (about 1,800 employees), cut marketing spend, and reduced costs overall.&nbsp;</p>\n <p>\"The COVID-19 pandemic and the impact of actions to mitigate the COVID-19 pandemic have materially adversely impacted and will continue to materially adversely impact our business, results of operations, and financial condition,\" the company said in the first of many risk factors listed in the S-1.</p> 2. Revenue growth is slowing, and the company expects it to continue to slow going forward. \n <figure> \n  <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e6fcfcbc485400f446d4847?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky, CEO and Co-founder of Airbnb, speaks to the Economic Club of New York at a luncheon at the New York Stock Exchange (NYSE) in New York, U.S. March 13, 2017.\" height=\"2110\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\"> \n   <figcaption>\n    Airbnb CEO Brian Chesky in 2017. \n    <p class=\"copyright\">Mike Segar/Reuters</p> \n   </figcaption> </img>\n </figure> \n <p>Airbnb enjoyed a meteoric rise in popularity, and it's unlikely to return to those levels of growth anytime soon.&nbsp;</p>\n <p>\"We have experienced significant revenue growth in the past,\" the company said. \"However, our revenue growth has slowed in recent periods and there is no assurance that historic growth rates will return.\"</p>\n <p>For the last three years, revenue growth has declined steadily, and it fell sharply in the first nine months of 2020.&nbsp;</p>\n <p>&nbsp;</p> 3. Laws and regulations regarding temporary home rental vary from region to region, and are always in flux, and that could hurt Airbnb's business. \n <figure> \n  <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/53d81dfb6da811ff6da608a2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbnb Stickers Protest\" height=\"1520\" width=\"2688\" charset=\"\"> \n   <figcaption>\n    Stickers on a building protesting Airbnb rentals. \n    <p class=\"copyright\">Joey Cosco/Business Insider</p> \n   </figcaption> </img>\n </figure> \n <p>Like Uber and other app-based startups that have exploded in popularity across the last decade, Airbnb has tangled with legislators and locals over how it does business.</p>\n <p>\"Since we began our operations in 2008, there have been and continue to be legal and regulatory developments that affect the short-term rental and home sharing business,\" the filing says. \"While we seek to work with governments, we have in the past, and are likely in the future to, become involved in disputes with government agencies regarding such laws and regulations.\"</p>\n <p>In some cases, like New York City, Airbnb says those regulations could result in a loss of revenue. In many cases, though, the laws simply do not exist yet to regulate short-term home rentals, and that means unknown risks.</p> 4. Airbnb is deeply in debt, to the tune of nearly $2 billion. \n <figure> \n  <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dc32d653afd372ad02f57a3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky Airbnb\" height=\"1961\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\"> \n   <figcaption> \n    <p class=\"copyright\">Eric Risberg/AP</p> \n   </figcaption> </img>\n </figure> \n <p>With a revenue of $2.52 billion and a net loss of $696.9 million for the first nine months of 2020, Airbnb isn't exactly stacking up a war chest. In fact, it's got just shy of $2 billion of principal on debts, and it's not totally certain it'll be able to pay interest and principal in the future.</p>\n <p>\"If we experience a decline in cash flow due to any of the factors described in these 'Risk Factors' or otherwise, we could have difficulty paying interest and the principal amount of our outstanding indebtedness,\" the filing says. \"If we are unable to generate sufficient cash flow or otherwise obtain the funds necessary to make required payments under our Credit Agreements, or if we fail to comply with the various requirements of our indebtedness, we could default under our Credit Agreements.\"</p> 5. The company has never earned a profit, and it lost more money during the first 9 months of the pandemic than it did in each of the previous 3 years. \n <figure> \n  <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3eaeba42f43f001ddfe11a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbnb Logo+ Stocks\" height=\"683\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\"> \n   <figcaption> \n    <p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/in-this-photo-illustration-an-airbnb-logo-seen-displayed-on-news-photo/1207431290?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Filip Radwanski/SOPA Images/LightRocket via Getty Images</a></p> \n   </figcaption> </img>\n </figure> \n <p>For Airbnb, the focus has always been on user acquisition and growth. That focus has come at the expense of becoming profitable, and there's no assurance that a solution to that issue is coming.</p>\n <p>\"We have incurred net losses in each year since inception, and we may not be able to achieve profitability,\" the filing says. \"We incurred net losses of $70.0 million, $16.9 million, $674.3 million, and $696.9 million for the years ended December 31, 2017, 2018, and 2019, and nine months ended September 30, 2020, respectively. Our accumulated deficit was $1.4 billion and $2.1 billion as of December 31, 2019 and September 30, 2020, respectively.\"</p>\n <p>This has been particularly worsened by the pandemic.</p>\n <p>\"In particular, we expect the ongoing economic impact from the COVID-19 pandemic to have a material adverse impact on our revenue and financial results for 2020 and beyond. While we have enacted measures to reduce our expenses, we expect to incur a significant net loss for 2020 as a result of the COVID-19 pandemic, and we are utilizing a significant portion of our cash to support our operations in 2020 resulting from a material decrease in bookings and revenue as compared to 2019.\"</p>\n <p><strong><a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1559720/000119312520294801/d81668ds1.htm\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"0fae4c9d0f1f14ba3a1ca48efd353b6b\">If you're interested in reading the full IPO filing, you can find it right here.</a></strong></p>\n <p><em><strong>Got a tip?</strong>&nbsp;Contact Business Insider senior correspondent Ben Gilbert via email (<a href=\"mailto:bgilbert@businessinsider.com\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">bgilbert@businessinsider.com</a>),</em><em>&nbsp;or Twitter DM (<a href=\"https://twitter.com/RealBenGilbert\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">@realbengilbert</a>). dn23@2020_6/2020/11/17/05-39-00-927_b35c3c5447315ab1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605591522093},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"How to vote in Georgia's US Senate runoff elections in January","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-vote-early-by-mail-georgia-senate-runoff-elections-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2d6111c741f0019aca13b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Warnock and Ossoff \" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Democratic candidate for Senate Jon Ossoff, right, and Democratic candidate for Senate Raphael G Warnock, left, arrive before they speak to a crowd during a &#34;Get Out the Early Vote&#34; event at the SluttyVegan ATL restaurant on Tuesday, Oct. 27, 2020, in Jonesboro, Ga.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Brynn Anderson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Georgia voters will decide control of the US Senate in two Senate runoff elections set to take place on January 5, 2021.&#160;</li>\n<li>In one race, first-term Republican David Perdue is facing Democrat Jon Ossoff.</li>\n<li>In the other, a special election, appointed Republican Senator Kelly Loeffler will face Democrat Raphael Warnock.&#160;</li>\n<li>Georgians have the option to vote by mail, early in-person, or on Election Day itself.</li>\n<li>Voters can request mail ballots now.</li>\n<li>The deadline to register to vote for the runoffs is Monday, December 7.</li>\n<li>The state will also hold 16 days of in-person early voting beginning on Monday, December 14.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>On January 5, 2021 Georgia will determine which party controls the US Senate <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-senate-runoff-elections-jon-ossoff-david-perdue-warnock-loeffler-2020-11\">with two runoff elections.&#160;</a></p><p>If no candidate in an election earns over 50% of the vote in Georgia, state law dictates that the top two vote-getters will advance to a runoff election. Georgia <a href=\"https://ballotpedia.org/Runoff_election\">is one of a dozen states</a>, most of which are in the South, that use runoff elections. In addition to the Senate races, a runoff for a Georgia Public Service Commissioner election <a href=\"https://www.wsbtv.com/news/politics/ga-secretary-state-moves-dec-1-state-runoffs-jan-5-coincide-with-crucial-senate-runoff/UG7JHSHDKVERTLD6OEKR5CYPMQ/\">will also take place on January 5.</a></p><p>In the state's regularly-scheduled US Senate election, first-term Republican <strong>David Perdue</strong> will go to a runoff against Democratic challenger <strong>Jon Ossoff</strong>, a 33-year-old former investigative journalist and US House staffer who ran in the high-profile 2017 special election for the US House in Georgia.</p><p>There's also a special US Senate election taking place to determine who will fill the seat held by former Sen. Johnny Isakson, who resigned in late 2019 over health concerns, and serve out the rest of his term until 2022.</p><p>Republican <strong>Kelly Loeffler</strong>, a wealthy businesswoman and WNBA team owner, was appointed to the seat after Isakson's resignation. After competing in a jungle special election with 20 other candidates, on November 3 she competed in a runoff against Democrat <strong>Raphael Warnock</strong>, a senior pastor at the famed Ebenezer Baptist Church in Atlanta.&#160;</p><p>Democrats will need to win both races in order to get to 50 seats in the Senate, which would allow Vice President-elect Kamala Harris to serve as the tie-breaking vote and give Democrats a narrow majority in the chamber.&#160;</p><p>Georgia voters made history this November <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-presidential-election-2020-live-vote-counts-results-2020\">in voting to hand the state's 16 Electoral College votes to President-elect Joe Biden</a>, making him the first Democratic presidential nominee to carry the state since former President Bill Clinton in 1992.&#160;</p><p>The former Republican bastion will now be the site of millions of dollars in outside spending and get-out-the-vote efforts. Here's how to vote in the runoff elections:&#160;</p><h2>When is the deadline to register to vote in Georgia?</h2><p>The deadline <a href=\"https://sos.ga.gov/index.php/Elections/register_to_vote\">to register to vote for the runoffs</a> is Monday, December 7.&#160;</p><p>Importantly, 17-year-old Georgians who will turn 18 by January 5 can register and vote too.</p><p>Georgia voters have the option <a href=\"https://sos.ga.gov/index.php/Elections/register_to_vote\">to register to vote</a> through the state's online portal, by mail with a paper application, or when applying for or renewing a driver's license at the DMV. You must be a US citizen and 18 years of age on Election Day to vote.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2d684402d49001924f36b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Gwinnett County \" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Officials work on ballots at the Gwinnett County Voter Registration and Elections Headquarters, Friday, Nov. 6, 2020, in Lawrenceville, near Atlanta.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/John Bazemore</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>When is the deadline to vote by mail?&#160;</h2><p>Any registered voter in Georgia can vote from home with a mail ballot without an excuse. Especially with COVID-19 cases <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/us/georgia-coronavirus-cases.html\">steadily rising in Georgia and nationwide as winter approaches</a>, voting by mail is a safe and convenient way to cast a ballot.</p><p>You can request your mail ballot now, either through the state's <a href=\"https://ballotrequest.sos.ga.gov/\">relatively new online request portal</a> or with a paper application mailed to your local elections office.</p><p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/stphnfwlr/status/1328064470548180999\">Over 620,000 voters,</a> most of whom are disabled, in the military and overseas, or voters aged 65 and above <a href=\"https://www.gpb.org/news/2020/09/02/nearly-800000-georgians-have-already-requested-absentee-ballots-for-november\">on the absentee rollover list</a>, are already set to receive mail ballots for the January runoffs.&#160;</p><p>If you plan to vote by mail, you should <strong>request your ballot now</strong>, or <strong>as soon as possible</strong>, and return it with plenty of time before Election Day. Election officials will begin sending out mail ballots to those who requested them <a href=\"https://sos.ga.gov/admin/files/2020%20Revised%20Short%20Calendar.pdf\">starting on Wednesday, November 18.&#160;</a></p><p>Domestic voters' mail ballots must be returned either by mail via the US Postal Service <a href=\"https://www.ajc.com/politics/where-are-absentee-ballot-drop-boxes-in-metro-atlanta/YWWVPFUDFZF5ZB6JLH5S33UIEU/\">or dropped off in-person</a> (in-person ballot return options vary by county) by the time the polls close on Election Day itself. Military and overseas ballots can be received up to three days after Election Day.&#160;&#160;</p><p>For the 2020 presidential election, the Postal Service recommended that voters request their mail ballots no later than 15 days before Election Day and mail their ballots back at least seven days out from the deadline. First-class mail takes two to five days to deliver each way.&#160;</p><p>Sending in your ballot as early as possible, however, will best ensure that your vote is properly received on time and counted.&#160;</p><h2>When does early voting begin?</h2><p>Georgia holds 16 days of early voting prior to every election. In-person early voting for the January 5 Georgia runoffs <a href=\"https://sos.ga.gov/admin/files/2020%20Revised%20Short%20Calendar.pdf\">will begin on Monday, December 14</a>, according to the Secretary of State's office.&#160;</p><p>The specific locations and hours for in-person early voting in each county have not yet been announced for the January 5 runoffs, but <a href=\"https://elections.sos.ga.gov/Elections/advancedVotingInfo.do\">will be available to find at this link.</a></p><h2>When is Election Day in the Georgia runoffs?</h2><p>The last day to vote in the Georgia Senate runoffs, Election Day, is on Tuesday, January 5, 2021. In-person voting locations and polling sites on Election Day open at 7:00 a.m. ET and close at 7 p.m. ET.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a would put precautions in place at gatherings, such as social distancing.</p><p>The findings come at odds with advice from public health experts, who are recommending Americans avoid small indoor gatherings, which are driving new COVID-19 cases in the US.</p><p>Dr. Iahn Gonsenhauser, chief quality and patient safety officer at The Ohio State University Wexner Medical Center, expressed concern on the impact these in-person gatherings could have on the rise in US infections.</p><p>\"We're going to look back at what happened during this holiday season and ask ourselves, 'Were we part of the solution or were we part of the problem?'\" Gonsenhauser said in a <a href=\"http://osuwmc.multimedia-newsroom.com/index.php/2020/11/12/survey-nearly-2-in-5-americans-will-likely-attend-large-holiday-gatherings/\">statement</a>.</p><p>\"When you're gathered together around the table, engaged in conversation, sitting less than 6 feet apart with your masks down, even in a small group, that's when the spread of this virus can really happen,\" he continued.</p><p>Top US infectious disease expert Dr. Anthony Fauci echoed the same concern in an October livestream with JAMA editor in chief Howard Bauchner, describing what people might expect as a result of large indoor Thanksgiving celebrations without proper health safety precautions put in place.</p><p>\"You get one person who's asymptomatic and infected, and then all of a sudden four or five people in that gathering are infected,\" Fauci told Bauchner. \"That's the exact scenario that you're going to see in Thanksgiving.\"</p><p>Gonsenhauser said the safest solution to ensure stemming the spread of the coronavirus among family members is to host virtual celebrations and cancel in-person plans. But if Thanksgiving celebrations will proceed in person, he emphasized the importance of social distancing in seating arrangements and encouraged people who are traveling to be mindful of COVID-19 restrictions.</p><p>\"If you have somebody in your household who's high risk and you're in a low incidence area, you're going to want to think twice about having a celebration where people are coming options for a military strike on Iran's main nuclear site, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/16/us/politics/trump-iran-nuclear.html?smid=tw-nytimes&smtyp=cur=cur\">The New York Times</a> reported on Monday.</p><p>Senior advisors ultimately discouraged Trump from pursuing the strike, arguing that such a move could spiral into a larger conflict with a short time remaining in the president's tenure, four current and former officials told The Times. Though Trump has refused to accept the results and concede, President-elect Joe Biden defeated him in the 2020 election.</p><p>Among those who persuaded Trump against moving forward with the strike were Vice President Mike Pence, Secretary of State Mike Pompeo, acting Defense Secretary Christopher Miller, and Joint Chiefs of Staff Chairman Gen. Mark A. Milley.</p><p>\"Thankfully, cooler heads prevailed,\" Nader Hashemi, director of the Center for Middle East Studies at the University of Denver, told Insider. \"A military strike on Iran would deeply destabilize an already unstable Middle East, with ripple effects across the region, especially in Iraq and Lebanon.\"</p><p>Furthermore, \"Iran is far away from having enough enriched uranium to build a bomb,\" Hashemi said. \"There is no imminent threat that would warrant a military strike.\"</p><p>The White House did not immediately respond to Insider's request for comment.</p><p>The reported Oval Office meeting took place just days after Trump <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-has-terminated-his-secretary-of-defense-after-losing-election-2020-11\">fired Defense Secretary Mark Esper</a>, and a day after international inspectors reported a major increase in Iran's uranium stockpile.</p><p>Iran's low-grade uranium stockpile is now <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-54912402\">more than 12 times the limit</a> set under <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/iran-nuclear-deal-explained\">the 2015 nuclear deal</a>, which Trump controversially withdrew the US from in May 2018.</p><p>Trump's decision to withdraw the US from the Obama-era nuclear accord rapidly raised tensions between Washington and Tehran, catalyzing a series of skirmishes in the Persian Gulf. The contentious dynamic was exacerbated in early 2020 after Trump ordered a drone strike that killed Iran's top general, Qassem Soleimani, while he was in Iraq.</p><p>The Soleimani strike pushed the US and Iran to the ,brink of war. Iran retaliated with a missile attack on US forces in Iraq that <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-pentagon-tbi-exclusive/more-than-100-u-s-troops-diagnosed-with-brain-injuries-from-iran-attack-idUSKBN2041ZK\">left dozens with serious injuries. </a>The US and Iran avoided a broader conflict in the aftermath of the Soleimani strike, but tensions remained high. The strike also led Iran to effectively abandon the 2015 nuclear deal altogether.</p><p>\"The only reason Iran didn't want to escalate beyond symbolic attacks at the time was precisely because it feared the US would escalate even further by striking inside the country,\" Hassan Hassan, program director of non-state actors and geopolitics at the Center for Global Policy, told Insider. \"If the US strikes inside Iran, and against nuclear facilities, then the gloves are off.\"</p><p><em>This story is breaking. Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li><strong>While not the same as a master's degree, a graduate certificate can offer some of the same career and skill-boosting benefits as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-decide-go-apply-graduate-school-now-pros-cons-2020-6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">grad school</a>, without the time commitment or cost. It can also be a stepping stone to eventually earning a full degree.</strong></li><li>Below are answers to frequently asked questions about graduate degrees, including how much they cost, how remote classes work, and how long they take.</li><li><strong>Read more: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/edx-vs-coursera-which-is-better-comparison\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Coursera and edX are two popular online learning platforms — here's how they compare in terms of price and programs offered</a></strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/insider-picks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up for Insider Reviews' weekly newsletter for more buying advice and great deals</a>.</strong></li></ul><p>As the pandemic continues, many people are wondering if <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-decide-go-apply-graduate-school-now-pros-cons-2020-6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">graduate school is a good investment of time and money right now</a>. While graduate degrees can provide chances to pivot to new careers, they also can take a few years to complete and charge high tuition, depending on the school and program.</p><p>While not the same as a master's degree, graduate certificates can sometimes be a more affordable option that requires less of a time commitment. Depending on the intended profession, they can help you learn new skills to transition into a different field — with official certification to show employers on LinkedIn or your resume — and some even have built-in portfolio assignments so you can exit the course with new samples of your work.</p><p>On some occasions, graduate certificates can double as college credits towards a related master's degree, since you technically completed graduate coursework. However, certificate credits are not automatically accepted by all schools — it varies on the university and program.</p><h3><strong>Here's everything you need to know about graduate certificates, how they compare to master's degrees, and some of the most popular graduate degree programs:</strong></h3><h2><strong>What's the difference between a graduate certificate and a degree?</strong></h2><p>Unlike finishing a full master's degree program, certificate program students take a few master's courses around a subject — like <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=EHFxW6yx8Uo&mid=40328&murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.coursera.org%2Fmastertrack%2Fsustainability-development-umichnt-umich\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Sustainability and Development</a> or <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fmicromasters%2Fuc-san-diegox-data-science-science\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Data Science</a> — and receive a certificate of completion upon passing the program.&#160;</p><p>Because certificates involve taking fewer classes (and don't usually have an admissions process), they're not considered the same as having a master's degree or PhD. However, they can help you stand out to prospective employers, especially if you're looking to transition into a different field and want to demonstrate that you learned the required skills.&#160;</p><h2><strong>How do I apply to a graduate certificate program?</strong></h2><p>Most certificate programs, such as the ones offered through <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/edx-affordable-online-micro-masters-programs-faq\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">edX's MicroMasters</a>, don't require a formal application process. If the course requires prerequisite knowledge, that information will usually be in the course description.</p><p>That being said, graduate certificate programs, such as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coursera-mastertrack-faq\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Coursera's MasterTracks</a>, can cap off after a certain number of applicants, so it's good to bookmark the enrollment date and sign up as soon as you can.</p><h2><strong>How much do they cost?</strong></h2><p>Graduate certificate programs can cost anywhere from $1,000 to $5,000, depending on the school, program, and length. The price of a graduate certificate can be a fraction of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/average-college-tuition#annual-average-tuition-at-public-4-year-colleges-and-universities\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the cost of traditional college degrees</a> (including online ones).</p><h2><strong>How long do certificate programs typically take?</strong></h2><p>Graduate certificate programs vary in length. Some, like <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fmicromasters%2Fmitx-supply-chain-managementnagement\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">MIT's Supply Chain Management MicroMasters</a>, can take a little over a year. Others, like the <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=EHFxW6yx8Uo&mid=40328&murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.coursera.org%2Fmastertrack%2Fux-design-minnesotainnesota\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">University of Minnesota's UX Design MasterTrack</a>, only take four months to complete.</p><h2><strong>Can I pick some of the classes in the certificate?</strong></h2><p>Usually, no. Coursera and edX's graduate certificate offerings pick the classes for you and you have to pass all of them to get the certification.</p><p>There are exceptions, though. <a href=\"https://www.extension.harvard.edu/academics/graduate-certificates\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Harvard's extension school</a>, for instance, lets you choose a few electives as part of your certificate.&#160;</p><h2><strong>How does grading work?</strong></h2><p>While graduate degree programs operate via GPAs, graduate certificates are often Pass/Fail. Coursera, for example, gives you a percentage grade on each assignment and then a final combined score.&#160;</p><p>Depending on the program and size of your class, your written feedback on assignments might also be shorter and more brief than it would be in a graduate degree program.</p><h2><strong>What if I want to get a master's degree after finishing a certificate program?</strong></h2><p>Specific programs in the <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fmicromastersomasters\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">edX MicroMasters</a> and <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=EHFxW6yx8Uo&mid=40328&murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.coursera.org%2Fmastertracktertrack\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Coursera MasterTrack</a> series have different guidelines regarding college credits. Some might only accept the certificate classes as college credits if you pursue a degree in the same school and program you completed the certificate in; others provide a list of schools that will take the credits.</p><p>One upside to completing a certificate before continuing a degree in the same field is that the certificate credits are typically cheaper and can save you some money down the line.</p><h2><strong>Can I get financial aid for a certificate program?</strong></h2><p>It depends. Coursera MasterTracks don't currently offer financial assistance. And while <a href=\"https://support.edx.org/hc/en-us/articles/215167877-What-courses-offer-financial-assistance-\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">edX lets you apply for financial aid</a> for most of its programs, for MicroMasters, you'll have to audit each course first and apply for financial aid every time.&#160;</p><h2>Bottom line:</h2><p>If you're looking to save time and money, graduate certificates can be a great alternative to graduate degrees, especially if you're just looking to pick up some new skills, such as accounting or coding. Online certificate programs can also offer some flexibility in terms of scheduling and can help you decide if you want to pursue a full degree later. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coursera-mastertrack-faq\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Here's a review of one of Coursera's MasterTrack programs</a>.</p><div Reference library for more stories</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul>\n<p>If you recently subscribed to HBO Max, you might be enjoying all the additional content that HBO has added to the new service.&#160;</p><p>But you might also have found that certain devices, like some smart TVs, don't have the HBO Max app.&#160;</p><p>All is not lost, though. If you have a Chromecast, you can watch HBO Max on any TV. All you'll need is that Chromecast, along with an iPhone, iPad, Android device, Mac, or PC.</p><h2><strong>How to cast HBO Max to a TV using Chromecast and your phone</strong></h2><p>Casting HBO Max from your phone to your TV is very straightforward. Be sure that your Chromecast <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-google-chromecast\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">is installed and working properly</a> — it should be connected to the same Wi-Fi network as your phone.&#160;</p><p><strong>1. </strong>Start the HBO Max app on your phone, and switch your TV to the input channel that the Chromecast is on.</p><p><strong>2. </strong>Select a show or movie to watch.</p><p><strong>3. </strong>Tap the Cast button at the top of the screen and then tap the Chromecast device you want to cast to.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ef508f44dca68069b26d1f9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to cast HBO Max to TV 1\" height=\"1242\" width=\"2688\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tap the Cast icon at the top of the HBO Max app and choose what device to cast to.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The HBO Max video should appear on your TV.</p><h2><strong>How to cast HBO Max to a TV using Chromecast and your computer</strong></h2><p>You can also cast HBO Max from your Mac or PC's Google Chrome browser.&#160;</p><p>Make sure that your Chromecast <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-google-chromecast\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">is installed and working properly</a>, and that it's connected to the same Wi-Fi network as your computer.&#160;</p><p><strong>1. </strong>Open HBO Max in a Chrome browser, and switch your TV to the input channel that the Chromecast is on.</p><p><strong>2. </strong>Select a show or movie to watch.&#160;</p><p><strong>3. </strong>Click the Cast icon (the very same one as seen on the mobile app) in your Google Chrome extensions toolbar. If you don't see it, click the three dots in the top-right and then select \"Cast\" from the menu that appears.</p><p><strong>4. </strong>Select the casting source/device from the pop-up menu.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2d94b402d49001924f386?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to cast HBO Max 1\" height=\"1438\" width=\"2880\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A list of available casting devices will appear.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abbey White/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The HBO Max show or movie should appear on your TV.</p><div likened it to the US's retreat from Vietnam in 1975.</p><p>Speaking on the Senate floor Monday afternoon, McConnell, who also <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/mitch-mcconnell-withdrawing-from-syria-is-a-grave-mistake/2019/10/18/c0a811a8-f1cd-11e9-89eb-ec56cd414732_story.html\">opposed</a> a withdrawal from Syria, stressed that the US must provide a \"limited but important role in defending American national security ... against terrorists who would like nothing more than for the most powerful force for good in the world to simply pick up our ball and go home.\"</p><p>\"A rapid withdrawal of US forces from Afghanistan now would hurt our allies and delight the people who wish us harm,\" McConnell said, adding that it would as \"humiliating\" as it was for US troops to withdraw from Saigon in the 1970s.</p><p>\"The consequences of a premature American exit would likely be even worse than President Obama's withdrawal from Iraq back in 2011, which fueled the rise of ISIS and a new round of global terrorism,\" McConnell added. Others, however, directly <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/robert-gates-isis-rise-2016-1\">link</a> ISIS's rise to the Syrian Civil War.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Trump had campaigned on withdrawing US troops from combat operations overseas, tweeting that US forces in Afghanistan would be \"home by Christmas!\"</p><p>On Friday, acting Defense Secretary Chris Miller issued a <a href=\"https://www.mcclatchydc.com/news/nation-world/national/national-security/article247175994.html\">memo</a> for Defense Department employees stating, \"it's time to come home,\" from the war against Al Qaeda. Miller left some room for interpretation, adding that the US must \"remain committed to finishing the war\" and \"avoid our past strategic error of failing to see the fight through to the finish.\"</p><p>McConnell's comments come as military officials ready themselves for an official directive from Trump as soon as this week, according to news <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/11/16/politics/trump-afghanistan-iraq-troop-drawdown-order/index.html\">reports</a>. Officials said they are preparing for a \"warning order\" to reduce their troop levels to 2,500 service members each in Iraq and Afghanistan, from the roughly 4,500 and 3,000 troops, respectively, CNN reported Monday.</p><p>McConnell's sentiment towards the potential drawdown has received similar concerns from House Republicans.&#160;</p><p>\"For the sake of the Afghan people, it is essential that the ongoing peace process be given the best chance for success,\" Republican Rep. Michael McCaul of Texas, the ranking member of the House Foreign Affairs Committee, said in a <a href=\"https://twitter.com/W7VOA/status/1328452132987686914?s=20\">statement</a>. \"A premature US withdrawal would not only jeopardize the Afghan government's ability to negotiate, but would endanger US counterterrorism interest.\"</p><p>The US's ongoing agreement with the Afghan government and the Taliban is contingent on a number of factors, including an overall reduction of violence. But following the ceasefire in February, violence in the country has dramatically spiked, prompting US officials to deliver a stark warning.</p><p>\"I return to the region disappointed that despite commitments to lower violence, it has not happened. Indeed, Pfizer announced last week that its COVID-19 vaccine had proven extremely effective in a late-stage trial, raising hopes of a faster return to normal than expected.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-crash-risks-momentum-stimulus-vaccine-complacency-peter-tchir-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-crash-risks-momentum-stimulus-vaccine-complacency-peter-tchir-2020-11\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">A Wall Street expert says the dramatic shift in stocks last week reeks of investor complacency — and warns that many favorite trades remain vulnerable to losses</a></em></p><p>Berkshire made several other changes to its portfolio. It added a $280 million stake in T-Mobile, and boosted its General Motors and Kroger holdings. On the other hand, the company trimmed its position in Apple — easily its biggest holding — by about 3.7% or 36 million shares.</p><p>The conglomerate also slashed its JPMorgan stake by more than 95%, from around 22 million shares worth more than $2 billion at the end of June to fewer than 1 million. It also sold more Wells Fargo shares, and exited a position in Costco that was worth more than $1.3 billion at the end of the second quarter.</p><p>Elsewhere, Berkshire cut its Barrick Gold position by more than 40%, despite only investing in the gold miner for the first time in the second quarter. It also reduced its holdings in PNC and M&#38;T Bank.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/goldman-sachs-energy-stocks-to-buy-now-market-recovery-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/goldman-sachs-energy-stocks-to-buy-now-market-recovery-2020-11\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Goldman Sachs says to load up on these 22 energy stocks set to soar as the market recovers — and details 10 to ditch</a></em></p><p>Close watchers of the company were <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-sold-apple-wells-fargo-shares-q3-david-kass-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">expecting significant changes</a> to Buffett's portfolio. Berkshire's <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-q3-earnings-stock-purchases-buybacks-2020-11-1029777502\">third-quarter earnings</a> showed $17.6 billion in stock purchases and $12.8 billion in stock sales, equating to $4.8 billion in net stock purchases in the period.</p><p>Moreover, Berkshire announced <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-19-billion-q3-investments-snowflake-dominion-2020-9-1029631281#\">$19 billion worth of investments last quarter</a>. Those included buying Bank of America and Snowflake stock, acquiring 5% stakes in five Japanese trading companies over the 12 months to August, and striking deals with Dominion Energy and Scripps.</p><p>Berkshire's roughly $6 billion in drug stocks and its flurry of other purchases <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-experts-analyze-strategy-caution-deals-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">signal a bullish turn</a> for Buffett and his team. After all, Berkshire <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-sells-jpmorgan-wells-fargo-buys-barrick-gold-2020-8-1029506182#\">slashed its financial holdings</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-sold-airline-stocks-april-2020-5-1029156875#\">sold its entire stakes</a> in the \"big four\" US airlines at connection.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ben Gilbert/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>You can download Nintendo Switch games from the Nintendo eShop in just a few minutes, depending on how fast your internet connection is.</li>\n<li>When you download a Nintendo Switch game, you can pay for it using a debit/credit card, a gift card, a PayPal account, or with Nintendo Points.&#160;</li>\n<li>If you happen to have a code, you can use it to download a game without paying.</li>\n<li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Digitally downloading <a href=\"http://bestbuy.7tiv.net/c/196318/614286/10014?subId1=bi_101719_download-nintendo-switch-games&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bestbuy.com%2Fsite%2Fnintendo-switch-32gb-console-neon-red-neon-blue-joy-con%2F6364255.p%3FskuId%3D63642554255\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nintendo Switch</a> games is an easy and efficient way to get all the games you want to play, without having to keep a collection of physical games.&#160;</p><p>Most Switch games can be downloaded within a few minutes, provided you have a fast internet connection, though large titles like \"The Legend of Zelda: Breath of the Wild\" may take several hours.</p><p>Downloading Switch&#160;games is easy — just make sure you have stable internet access, and can keep the console connected to its charger while you're downloading. You'll also need to have enough space to store the games you download, which might mean adding extra storage space with an SD card or external hard drive.</p><h2><strong>How to download Nintendo Switch games from the Nintendo eShop</strong></h2><p><strong>1. </strong>From the Switch homescreen, navigate down to the eShop icon on the bottom task bar — it looks like an orange shopping bag — and press A to open it. Enter your account password if prompted.</p><p><strong>2. </strong>In the eShop, you can choose to search for games by name, browse among recent releases, or look at the best sellers. There's also a \"Great Deals\" option that will show you all the games currently on sale. Once you choose a game to download, click on it with A.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da8a956cc4a0a25a919b1ff?format=jpeg\" alt=\"IMG_6041\" height=\"1306\" width=\"2860\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The eShop makes it easy to find games you already know about, or to browse through new titles.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Steven John/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>3. </strong>Scroll over to the box labeled \"Proceed to Purchase\" (or \"Free Download\" if the game is free) and press A.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da8a9f54af90978884f445b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"IMG_6042\" height=\"1313\" width=\"2798\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Every game has its own information page, where you can check out pictures and videos.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Steven John/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4. </strong>There are several ways to pay for a game. You can use Nintendo Points, which you earn from buying other games (each point is worth one cent), use a debit or credit card, an eShop gift card, or a PayPal account. Clicking on any option will give you instructions for how to link that payment type to your account.</p><p><strong>5. </strong>Once you've linked your payment method and added funds to your account, confirm that you want to make the purchase.</p><p><strong>6. </strong>The eShop will take a moment to process your purchase. Once it does, just sit back and wait while your new game downloads onto the system.</p><h2><strong>How to download Nintendo Switch games with a code</strong></h2><p>If you've received a download code for a Nintendo Switch game — for example, if you bought a digital game code from Amazon — then you can load the game onto your console without any need for extra payment.</p><p><strong>1. </strong>Again, open the eShop by selecting its icon from the Switch homescreen.</p><p><strong>2. </strong>In the menu on the left side of the screen, scroll to the bottom and select \"Enter Code.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da8ab314af90979c53967a2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"IMG_6043\" height=\"1392\" width=\"2948\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>If you have a code, you can enter into the textbox here.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Steven John/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>3. </strong>Press A or tap the empty text box to bring up a keyboard.</p><p><strong>4. </strong>Enter in your code and press \"OK\" or the plus button.</p><p><strong>5. </strong>If your code is valid, you'll be shown what game the code is tied to.</p><p><strong>6. </strong>The game will begin to download.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5da0bf874af909707f7a61aa\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe Boockvar's office argued that the lawsuit was filed \"on the basis of repeatedly rejected legal theories and no evidence.\"</p><p>Last week, the law firm representing the Trump campaign in the case, Porter Wright Morris &#38; Arthur, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/nov/13/trump-law-firm-withdraws-pennsylvania-election-case\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">moved to withdraw</a> from it. Hearings in the case are set for Tuesday and Thursday.</p><p>President-elect Joe Biden won the 2020 election by flipping Pennsylvania and the upper midwestern battleground states of Michigan and Wisconsin. The Trump campaign has filed lawsuits in Pennsylvania and Michigan and demanded a recount in Wisconsin.</p><p>As of Monday, Biden's lead in Pennsylvania is nearly 70,000 votes, and it's unlikely any of the Trump campaign's lawsuits will result in a reversal of Trump's loss in the state.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
