13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"How to share your ETA in the Apple Maps app on your iPhone","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-share-eta-in-apple-maps-iphone","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d8cd6f32e22af5c8b0b24ac?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple Maps\" height=\"1800\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can now share your ETA in Apple Maps with people in your contacts list with the new iOS 13 software update.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>To share your ETA in the Apple Maps app on your iPhone, you'll need to tap the \"Share ETA\" button, which appears once you start navigating.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Apple Maps can share your ETA with anyone in your contacts list, and anyone you've shared with will be able to track your progress in real time.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>ETA stands for \"estimated time of arrival,\" and tracks when you're expected to arrive at your destination.</strong></li>\n<li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>The ETA (estimated time of arrival) feature in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/apple-maps\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Apple Maps</a>&#160;lets you give your friends a real-time window into your route and location — that way, they don't have to wonder when you will arrive.&#160;</p><p>When you share your ETA, your contacts will be able to see where your iPhone is, and track you along your route.</p><p>Note that this feature isn't available in the Maps app on <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-version-of-ios-do-i-have\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">an iPhone running iOS 12 or earlier</a>.&#160;</p><h2><strong>How to share your ETA in Apple Maps on an iPhone </strong></h2><p><strong>1. </strong>Open the Apple Maps app and find your destination.&#160;</p><p><strong>2. </strong>If you haven't already started directions to a location, tap the blue \"Directions\" button. Type in the location address, choose your preferred route and tap the green \"GO\" button to start navigation.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da9d148cc4a0a5ee0366c95?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to share ETA in Apple Maps iPhone\" height=\"2208\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tap the blue &#34;Directions&#34; button.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Laura McCamy/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>3. </strong>While navigating, tap the gray line at the bottom of your screen to reveal menu options, including \"Share ETA.\"&#160;</p><p><strong>4. </strong>Tap the \"Share ETA\" button.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da9d195cc4a0a5f12346347?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to share ETA in Apple Maps iPhone\" height=\"2208\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tap the &#34;Share ETA&#34; icon.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Laura McCamy/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>5. </strong>When you tap the \"Share ETA\" icon, Maps pulls up your five most recent contacts. Tap any one of those to share your ETA with that person. You can share your ETA with more than one person at a time.</p><p><strong>6. </strong>If you want to share your ETA with someone who isn't in your five most recent contacts, tap the \"Contacts\" icon to search for that person. Tap the contact on the list to start sharing.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da9d1e7cc4a0a5f675eb032?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to share ETA in Apple Maps iPhone\" height=\"2208\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can also tap the &#34;Contacts&#34; button is the person you want to share your ETA with is not in your top five recent contacts.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Laura McCamy/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>7. </strong>While you have sharing on, you'll see a notice at the bottom of your screen that reminds you that you have sharing on and how many people you have shared with.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da9d249cc4a0a5ff3151ad5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to share ETA in Apple Maps iPhone\" height=\"2208\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The message at the bottom of your screen lets you know how many people you&#39;re sharing your ETA with.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Laura McCamy/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>8. </strong>The icon of each person you're sharing with will have a blue ring around it in the Share ETA screen. To stop sharing with someone, simply tap their icon to end sharing.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5da9d2a2cc4a0a6054478866?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to share ETA in Apple Maps iPhone\" height=\"2208\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tap the contact that you&#39;d like to stop sharing your ETA with.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Laura McCamy/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>There are some limitations on sharing your ETA in Apple's Maps app. You need to be actively using the app for navigation. It also only works for driving directions — walking and transit don't have the ETA option, and Apple doesn't include biking directions.&#160;</p><p>Most importantly, you can only share your ETA with people in your contacts list, so be sure to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-add-contacts-to-iphone\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">add people to your contacts</a> before you try to share ETA.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5d8e19fb2e22af18f40d281d\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5d8e19fb2e22af18f40d281d&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><h2><strong>Related coverage from&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" src=\"https://cdn.jwplayer.com/players/qYy8iMwj-jZbcmOYf.html\"\nwidth=\"100%\" height=\"100%\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"auto\" title=\"How to stay safe at work during the COVID-19 pandemic\"\nstyle=\"position:absolute;\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>As the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/covid-19\">novel coronavirus</a> continues to spread, more and more cities are escalating their tactics to keep the virus at bay.</li>\n<li>Cities have asked people to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-one-week-enforce-social-distancing-flatten-curve-coronavirus-2020-3\">socially distance</a> and, in some cases, to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-aerial-photos-san-francisco-abandoned-schools-shelter-in-place-2020-3\">shelter in place</a>.</li>\n<li>But some are not lucky enough to work from home. <a href=\"https://www.northwell.edu/find-care/find-a-doctor/emergency-medicine/dr-eric-christopher-cioe-pena-md-11363430\">Dr. Eric Cioe-Pena, an emergency physician and the director of global health for Northwell Health</a>, gave us some tips for staying safe at work.</li>\n<li>Dr. Pena says washing your hands is more effective than hand sanitizer, and recommends wiping down common areas like keyboards and phones.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><em>Following is a transcript of the video.</em></p><p><strong>Narrator:</strong> As the novel coronavirus continues to spread, more and more cities are escalating their tactics to keep the virus at bay, asking people to socially distance, and, in some cases, to shelter in place. But some are not so lucky to have the ability to work from home. Dr. Eric Cioe-Pena, an emergency physician and the director of global health for Northwell Health, gave us some tips for staying safe at work.</p><p><strong>Eric Cioe-Pena:</strong> The No. 1 thing to do is wash your hands. Either 20 seconds with soap and water or with a hand sanitizer that's greater than 60% alcohol, because the main mode of transmission is gonna be touching surfaces that someone has coughed or sneezed on and then touching your face. So, that's your first line of defense, is handwashing.</p><p>So, comparing hand sanitizer to soap and water, if you have the ability to use soap and water, that's your best bet. So, hand sanitizer is a quick way to disinfect your hands in between soap-and-water washes, but soap and water really does have a greater efficacy in washing away droplets, washing away viral particles, and removing any soil or contaminants on your hands where virus could be hidden underneath. Hand sanitizer essentially is a superficial clean, so if you've got no dirt and no grime on your hands and you use hand sanitizer, it is effective at killing most things that are on your hands, but anytime you have any type of dirt or anything else where something could be hiding underneath that layer of dirt, hand sanitizer isn't gonna get it, but water and soap will. I also recommend, at the beginning of the day, wiping down areas that you're gonna touch often in your work area. So, keyboards, phones, mouse I would disinfect with any household or business disinfectant would work.</p><p>One of the other ways to catch the virus is to be in close contact with other people. Being next to another human being for greater than two minutes within six feet who is sick and showing symptoms definitely is a risk. The idea right now is you wanna practice some social distancing between people so that if someone is sick, we're not within six feet of them as much as possible. The other thing is avoiding gatherings of, you know, greater than five people that aren't absolutely essential to business is probably a good temporary measure at this point.</p><p><strong>Narrator:</strong> But social distancing is not always feasible, especially when your work involves person-to-person contact.</p><p><strong>Cioe-Pena:</strong> So, the service industry is a tough area. They're especially tough because they also don't have any sick time off, and if they don't work they're not making money, so that's something that society, in general, we have to take a look at, because they really do have kind of a financial imperative to work even while sick. So, the worst thing someone in the service industry could do is work while sick. But the things that they can do to protect themselves: disinfect their hands, make sure that every time they're touching someone else's credit card, touching a check, touching something that another human being has touched in the course of their job, that before they do anything like, certainly, eat or touch their face, that they're disinfecting with soap and water or hand sanitizer.</p><p>The handshake is a tough thing 'cause it's really ingrained in our culture, right. I mean, you know, even now when I'm meeting people, part of me is, like, resisting the urge to extend my hand out and shake people's hands. So I think having something that's a gesture, the elbow is certainly, I think, the safer thing than the fist bump, just having that momentary contact with an area that's not gonna go anywhere near your face. You know, even just kind of a slight nod or a bow oftentimes will get kind of the job done.</p><p>We need to keep calm. We have to kind of take this with the appropriate level of seriousness, protect the people that are at risk of having worse outcomes, but the rest of us need to just kind of take the anxiety down one notch, realize that we're gonna get through this, it's gonna be here, it's gonna pass through our communities, and so we really just need to kind of do things that are smart, but try to avoid panic.</p><p><em>EDITOR'S NOTE: This video was originally published in March 2020.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a My secret weapon is my gift of gab.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/porn-star-making-five-figures-from-home-during-pandemic-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3eb365cdf25a001e84e7ed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Romi Rain\" height=\"2250\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rain says that at 32 years old, she&#39;s considered a veteran in the porn industry.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Romi Rain</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Romi Rain (not her real name) is a 32-year-old adult film star who lives and works in Southern California.</li>\n<li>She began doing nude modeling at the age of 19 before becoming an exotic dancer at a strip club. From there, she started webcamming, and at the age 25, signed with an agency to perform in adult films.</li>\n<li>Since porn isn't a \"forever career,\" Rain says many adult performers find ways to make residual income on the side by uploading content to websites like OnlyFans.</li>\n<li>Rain films and edits her own content, which can range from elaborate video shoots to simply live-streaming playing video games on Twitch. During the pandemic, she says she's making at least five figures a month.</li>\n<li>This is her story, as told to freelance writer Jenny Powers.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The porn industry isn't regulated, so there was no official shutdown when COVID-19 hit. Filming stopped here in California the third week in March but it was more like a polite suggestion — it's not like we're part of the Screen Actor's Guild or anything. Still, when businesses and restaurants are forced to close their doors, it's probably not the best time to shoot a gang bang.&#160;</p><h2><strong>The average lifespan in the adult film industry for a woman is two to five years.</strong></h2><p>Anything beyond that and you're considered a veteran, like me. I was 25 when I started doing hardcore porn, which is considered old to first get started, and I'm 32 now.</p><p>When I was 19 years old I did some doing freelance nude modeling for a site called Model Mayhem. I loved modeling and dancing so much that I literally woke up one day and went to an audition at a nude club called 4Play in Los Angeles and became an exotic dancer. I credit my early strip club days with learning how important a conversation and setting a mood can be. Personally, I never sat on laps. I always sat next to someone and started a genuine conversation. Then if we wound up in the VIP room, boundaries and respect had long been established.&#160;&#160;</p><p>I was still modeling and dancing when I got hit up to do skits and games for \"The Playboy Morning Show,\" which led to being on the cam site Playboy Live when I was 23, which was so much fun. From there, I did work for Playboy TV, which was technically my first soft porn experience. I started doing solos for a couple of websites and shot a centerfold for Hustler magazine that was released in 2013. By then I was 25, and I contacted a well-known industry agency to start repping me. That's when I began working in adult film, and the rest is history.</p><h2><strong>I'm very vocal about what I will and won't do at my job.</strong></h2><p>Some of my nos include being suspended in air or allowing anyone to repeatedly slap me in the face. I also have a list of the only 20-30 guys I'm willing to work with. I'm known as a diva in the industry, but at the end of the day, I'm just protecting myself. The #MeToo movement and social media has given us the ability to say no more often and helped make the industry safer by outing people for their bad behavior.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3eb222cdf25a001e84e7dc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Adult actress Romi Rain posing with her poster for Cam4, an adult website.\" height=\"1680\" width=\"2240\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rain posing with her poster modeling for Cam4, an adult website.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Romi Rain</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>I have no regrets getting into the business; it's led me to a better life than I ever expected. I have to say, cam girls were really ahead of the curve, because content truly is king.</p><p>More than anything, this pandemic has proved our worth as content-creators. I run my own 18+ website and I'm a brand ambassador for Cam4. I'm also on Pornhub, OnlyFans, MiniVids, Clips for Sale, and even play video games over live-stream on Twitch. I'm a one-woman show when it comes to content creation: I do my own filming, editing, and uploading. It's an amazing time to interact with people directly, and it's helped humanize us more as performers. My secret weapon as an adult entertainer is my gift of gab. I love chatting and long-winded dirty talk definitely takes a degree of skill and creativity.&#160;</p><h2><strong>People are often surprised to learn that porn is a day job. It's pretty much 9-to-5 work.</strong></h2><p>Like any other job, what you put in is what you get out, and if you're enjoying yourself too much, you're probably not doing your job to the best of your ability.&#160;&#160;</p><p>As actors, we are responsible to get and pay for a full panel of urine and blood tests every 14 days to ensure we're healthy. It costs $165 each time and insurance doesn't cover it. In most instances, we're also responsible to pay for our wardrobe. A guy can wear the exact same shirt in a dozen scenes, but women need head to toe new everything every scene, so we've got a lot more overhead expenses.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3eb546cdf25a001e84e7fd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Romi Rain 1\" height=\"1650\" width=\"2200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rain says that female performers have a lot more expenses than males — like nails, hair, makeup, and buying new outfits.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Romi Rain</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Before COVID-19, an average workday involved waking up early to shower, shave, and groom. Upon arrival at the shoot house, there's paperwork to complete, then I usually get my makeup done. After, we do still shots known as 'pretty girls' and sex stills with other performers. The sex scenes themselves are highly technical and each position takes between two to five minutes. Afterward, there might be more photos, and then to sign out you hold up your ID verifying your age and legal name on camera, and give verbal consent that you performed at your own free will and were treated fairly.&#160;</p><h2><strong>My longest shoot was eight days for a feature, and a few of those days went into double-digit hours.&#160;</strong></h2><p>Performers are paid a flat rate per scene. Often, though, you're just hired for one scene at a time on a 9-to-5 schedule.</p><p>Women are paid a bit more per scene ($700 to $3,000 depending on what the scene requires) but men can work more because there are more females to choose from. More elaborate, detailed home shoots can take hours to set-up, break down, upload, and edit.</p><p>It's good and bad being able to work as much or as little as I want to because some days I feel like I could be doing more, but it's incredibly important to take breaks.&#160;</p><p>My monthly income is five figures — how high those five figures go really depends on me. I feel like the pandemic makes customers even more eager for content at all hours of the day and night, because they're anxious and bored and want to get their mind off the state of the world.</p><p>I'm not sure when, but I have no doubt the porn industry will bounce back. I mean, <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/chart/16959/share-of-the-internet-that-is-porn/\">nearly a quarter of mobile internet searches</a> are for pornographic content. Millions of people consume our content daily, and despite us all being treated like 'she who shall not be named,' people know and like us, that's for sure. An independent group of experts found signs of effectiveness after reviewing data from an ongoing 30,000-person trial, Moderna said. The company plans to apply for emergency use authorization later this month.</p><p>The encouraging news comes one week after <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pfe-stock\">Pfizer</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/btnx-stock\">BioNTech</a> revealed similarly positive results from their own vaccine trial. While both experimental drugs still require regulatory approval to be distributed, their effectiveness suggests the virus could be reliably contained sooner than expected.</p><p><strong>Here's where US indexes stood at the 4 p.m. ET market close on Monday:</strong></p><ul><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">S&#38;P 500</a>:</strong> 3,626.91, up 1.2%</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/dow_jones?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dow Jones industrial average</a>:</strong> 29,950.44, up 1.6% (471 points)</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nasdaq_composite?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nasdaq composite</a>:</strong> 11,924.13, up 0.8%</li></ul><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-cheap-companies-value-economic-rebound-goldman-2020-11\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"\">GOLDMAN SACHS: Buy these 20 deeply underpriced stocks now before the recovery helps them rebound and crush Wall Street's low expectations in 2021</a></em></p><p>The energy and industrial sectors led the S&#38;P 500 higher. Health care and real estate stocks lagged the broader market's gains.</p><p>The so-called <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/airline-cruise-stocks-moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-data-market-reopening-recovery-2020-11-1029806318\">reopening trade soared</a> as Moderna's update lifted investor optimism. Airlines including <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ual-stock\">United</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/aal-stock\">American</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/dal-stock\">Delta</a> gained, as did cruise lines. Hotel stocks also jumped as investors bet on near-term vaccine distribution to revive the struggling sector.</p><p>Conversely, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/zoom-peloton-wfh-stock-prices-moderna-covid-vaccine-trial-2020-11-1029806091\">stocks that thrived in the stay-at-home economy sank</a> as investors positioned for a full recovery. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/zm-stock\">Zoom</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nflx-stock\">Netflix</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pton-stock\">Peloton</a>, among others, tumbled. Falling tech giants in particular led the Nasdaq composite to underperform peer indexes.</p><p>\"The global population couldn't have asked for more from the Moderna vaccine,\" Seema Shah, chief strategist at Principal Global Investors, said. \"Visibility towards a return to normality is increasing, and this should provide more fuel to the reflation rally, with small caps, value, and cyclicals clear beneficiaries.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-how-peter-kraus-built-firm-where-to-invest-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Former AllianceBernstein CEO Peter Kraus outlines how he has built his disruptive boutique from a 'concept' into a 50-person, $3 billion firm in just 2 years — and shares the 3 areas he is looking at for investing opportunities</a></em></p><p>Moderna's update offset concerns about still-rising COVID-19 cases throughout the US. The country reported more than 139,000 new cases on Sunday along with nearly 69,000 new hospitalizations, according to <a href=\"https://covidtracking.com/data\">The COVID Tracking Project</a>. Multiple cities have reinstated economic restrictions to hinder the virus's spread. With the pace of economic recovery already slowing, prolonged lockdowns risk freezing the nation's rebound.</p><p>Monday's strong open comes after Pfizer's own vaccine announcement spurred a massive rotation to value stocks throughout last week. Major indexes notched <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-vaccine-coronavirus-hopes-offset-virus-spike-2020-11-1029802604\">a second-straight weekly gain</a>&#160;as investors bet on near-term vaccine distribution.</p><p>BlackRock strategists said Monday that&#160;the distribution of a vaccine could make the coronavirus recession <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/coronavirus-economic-impact-outlook-financial-crisis-2008-comparison-blackrock-2020-11-1029807744\">far less devastating than the financial crisis</a> and its long-term scarring. Though rising cases may drive short-term turbulence, the two promising vaccine candidates signal the pandemic can soon come to an end, the team said.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/where-to-invest-in-2021-themes-driving-markets-goldman-sachs-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Goldman Sachs unveils the top 10 themes it expects to drive the markets in 2021 — and shares where to invest your money</a></em></p><p>\"Positive news on COVID-19 vaccines gives us greater confidence that the economic restart can re-accelerate in 2021,\" the strategists said in a&#160;<a href=\"https://www.blackrock.com/corporate/insights/blackrock-investment-institute/publications/weekly-commentary\">weekly report</a>. \"We prefer to look through any market volatility generated by the virus resurgence and renewed restrictions over the challenging months ahead.\"</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/pfizer-astrazeneca-stock-price-moderna-covid19-vaccine-shows-strong-efficacy-2020-11-1029806658\">Pfizer and BioNTech both plunged</a> on the vaccine news. Moderna's experimental vaccine can be stored at refrigerator temperatures for up to 30 days, making it far easier to transport than the Pfizer drug that needs to be stored at -94 degrees Fahrenheit.</p><p>Spot <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/gold-price\">gold</a> fell as much as 1.3%, to $1865.30 per ounce, as investors rotated out of safe-haven assets. The precious metal pared losses through the morning.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stocks-buy-stay-at-home-stock-picks-post-pandemic-barclays-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Barclays details its ultimate strategy for picking stay-at-home market winners for a post-COVID world — and shares 2 stocks all investors should own before the recovery accelerates</a></em></p><p>The US dollar declined against a basket of 10 major currency peers and Treasury yields climbed.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">Bitcoin</a> climbed as much as 6.3%, to $16,854.98, as its weeks-long rally continued. The world's most popular cryptocurrency <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-16000-cryptocurrency-market-rally-btc-highest-years-paypal-2020-11-1029796564\">surged above the $16,000 resistance level</a> on Thursday.</p><p>Oil prices gained on hopes for a vaccine to revive travel activity and overall consumption. <a It wasn't because of train delays or because I lost my watch. It was just so much harder getting out of bed since I'd started sleeping on <a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/Rd6zg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Tuft &#38; Needle's Mint Mattress</a>.&#160;</p><p>It's the second mattress from Tuft &#38; Needle, which has three mattresses in total. It'll quickly wrap you up in its soft and comfortable embrace. If you want to try to get work done while sitting in this bed, here's my recommendation: don't. My experience with the mattress is that you'll simply end up horizontal, slumped into an impromptu nap.</p><h2>Specs</h2><p><a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/Rd6zg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d139d08e3ecba044b5d38d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"tuft and needle mint mattress 2\" height=\"1960\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Connie Chen/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>The Mint mattress is an upgrade from the company's <a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/MdNPK\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">best-selling original mattress</a>, a 10-inch, medium-firm mattress with almost 6,000 five-star reviews on Amazon and more than 100,000 total reviews on the <a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/70JEy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Tuft &#38; Needle website</a>.&#160;</p><p>Comparatively, the <a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/Rd6zg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\">Mint Mattress</a> is a little thicker at 12 inches tall, but also softer, cooler, and better for pressure relief. The company recommends the Mint if you're a side sleeper or you run hot while sleeping. With more support on its sides, the Mint is also good if you often sit on the edge of your bed.&#160;</p><h2>Set-up process</h2><p>The mattress comes rolled up and packed tightly in a box. I tested the Full size, which weighed 66 pounds and admittedly wasn't fun to carry up the stairs of my fourth-floor walk-up (another set of hands will definitely help if you live in a similar situation). However, once I got the mattress up to my room, the rest of the set-up process was much easier.&#160;</p><p>After I cut through the plastic wrap, the mattress unfurled and rose to its full size. Though the company says there may be a new mattress smell, I personally didn't notice one. Regardless, this potential smell is a result of the packaging process, not chemicals. The mattress is CertiPUR-US and Greenguard Gold certified, so it's free from harmful chemicals and gases.&#160;</p><h2>Review of the Tuft &#38; Needle Mint mattress</h2><p>I positioned the mattress on my new <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/zinus-shawn-bed-frame-review\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Zinus bed frame</a>, threw on <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/primary-goods-percale-sheets-review\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one of my favorite sheet sets</a>, and slept on it that same night. Tuft &#38; Needle gives you 100 nights to test out its mattresses risk-free. If you don't end up liking it, you'll get a free refund and the company will also coordinate free pickup and send it to a donation location of your choice.&#160;</p><p>I, for one, never returned my <a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/Rd6zg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\">Mint Mattress</a>. It's incredibly comfortable, supportive, and adaptive to both the way my body moves and the changing temperatures of my room.&#160;</p><p>The mattress features Tuft &#38; Needle's signature Adaptive Foam, which contours to your body and provides pressure relief like memory foam but is also breathable and bouncy like latex. This top-layer construction combines all the features many sleepers look for and is what also makes the original mattress and its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tuft-and-needle-pouch-bean-bag-review-2018-7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Pouch bean bag chair</a> (no longer available) so invitingly comfortable.</p><p><a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/Rd6zg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d13a3e9e3ecba0f2241e1d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"tuft and needle mint mattress 3\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tuft &#38; Needle</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>In the <a href=\"https://tuftandneedle.attfm2.net/Rd6zg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\">Mint Mattress</a>, the Adaptive Foam is further enhanced by 30% more graphite, which maximizes its cooling abilities. Meanwhile, \"open-cell foam technology\" allows air to flow freely through the mattress and improves breathability, so you won't overheat like you would on a memory foam mattress.</p><p>Even as the weather got exponentially hotter during the summer, my body hasn't while sleeping on this mattress. It has a soft and thick knit cover with a bit of texture you can feel through your sheets — cozy and comforting, and something that sounds perfect for colder temperatures. But surprisingly, this cover doesn't get overwhelming or hot in the summer, and that's because of the rest of the mattress' cooling and breathable design.</p><p>Between the Adaptive Foam layer and base layer, there's a transition layer filled with gel beads that add more support. The base layer is the most firm and gives better edge support. Instead of sinking downwards every time I roll too close to the edge or I perch on my bed putting on my shoes, the mattress seems unaffected by the shift in weight.</p><p>The core of the mattress is of course also supportive. I sleep in all sorts of positions (side, stomach, back), and each feels comfortable. I've found that I'm also able to rest on my side for long periods of time than on my previous mattress. If you sleep with a partner, the mattress is firm and adaptive enough that you won't disturb the entire bed when you reposition yourself or get out of bed early in the morning. Overall, the mattress simply feels stable yet comforting, which is exactly what you want to collapse into at the end of a long day.&#160;</p><h2>The bottom line&#160;</h2><p>My first introduction to Tuft &#38; Needle was its Pouch bean bag chair, which remains one of my favorite products I've ever tested. I shouldn't have been surprised that its flagship mattress would be a hit too. From the very first night, it proved to be supportive, breathable, and comfortable, and it's been consistently so in the year months I've been testing it.</p><div +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5d13a3e9e3ecba0f2241e1d7?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"6750dc19f8ad7ffc4d02ae0fa6785b62","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn7@2020_6/2020/11/17/05-38-42-651_2fa946bd0440e51f.webp","destWidth":800,"destHeight":600,"sourceBytes":56580,"destBytes":56580,"author":"cchen@businessinsider.com (Connie Chen)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5d13991ce3ecba1e4e095cab?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn67@2020_5/2020/11/17/05-38-59-468_13aee552233c828e.webp","https://i.insider.com/5d139d08e3ecba044b5d38d7?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn64@2020_2/2020/11/17/05-38-58-292_90c2c32510a1c07d.webp","https://i.insider.com/5d13a3e9e3ecba0f2241e1d7?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn7@2020_6/2020/11/17/05-38-42-651_2fa946bd0440e51f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn44@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-39-00-474_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=1y8WPXfJlPg:AOaJlWBYRXU:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn3@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-38-57-243_fd3fd21f7c24ab0f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=1y8WPXfJlPg:AOaJlWBYRXU:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn80@2020_4/2020/11/17/05-38-57-074_d794951afd3f8378.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-53-238_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=1y8WPXfJlPg:AOaJlWBYRXU:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn79@2020_4/2020/11/17/05-39-01-728_7100254bbb7323e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/1y8WPXfJlPg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn84@2020_6/2020/11/17/05-38-46-731_8fc5bcec27434594.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605591522122},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"Preferred stocks supply steady dividends to investors — here's how to evaluate them for your portfolio","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-preferred-stock","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2fe3b402d49001924f476?format=jpeg\" alt=\"preferred stocks\" height=\"1500\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Preferred stock shares pay higher dividends and their prices are less volatile.\n<p class=\"copyright\">seksan Mongkhonkhamsao/ Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Preferred stock is a type of equity (ownership) security issued by companies to raise money.</li>\n<li>Preferred stocks pay a higher, fixed dividend than common stock, but their share prices don't appreciate as much as common shares do.&#160;</li>\n<li>Preferreds are best for institutional investors or sophisticated individuals who want them for tax reasons and can weather the risk of the shares being recalled.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\"><strong>Visit Business Insider's Investing Reference library for more stories</strong></a><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\"><strong>.</strong></a></li>\n</ul><p>Publicly traded companies have a few ways to raise money. The usual methods include issuing common stock — part-ownership in a company that often rewards buyers with regular payments, called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-a-dividend\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">dividends</a> — and selling <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-a-corporate-bond\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">corporate bonds</a>, loans that come with contractual interest payments, and the full repayment when the bond finally matures.&#160;</p><p>And then there's a third option: preferred stock, which somewhat confusingly mashes up features of both common stock and bonds. The name's kind of a misnomer — preferred stock shares aren't \"preferred\" because they're extra-fancy. Nor are they \"better\" than common stock, except under limited circumstances and for certain types of investors.&#160;</p><p>If you're wondering whether preferred stocks are right for your portfolio, here's what you need to know.&#160;</p><h2><strong>What is preferred stock?</strong></h2><p>As with common stock, when you buy a share of preferred stock, you are buying a (small) part of the company. And also like common stock, you usually get a certain percentage of money on a regular basis — that's the dividend. The dividend comes from a portion of the company's profits, assuming there are any.&#160;</p><p>Unlike common stock, preferred stock comes with limited or no voting rights — you can't use your share to vote for the board of directors, or for or against other policies.&#160;</p><p>Because preferreds don't come with those voting rights, companies sometimes issue them instead of common stock to avoid diluting ownership. Preferred shares can be sold to qualified investors and employees by privately held companies as well as public ones; if the company goes public, any preferreds can then be bought and sold on a stock exchange.</p><p>The price of a preferred share goes up and down based on demand, like common stock. But that share price doesn't wander away too far from its par value — that is, its initial offering price. It generally moves in response to general interest rates, much like bond prices do.</p><p>That's because preferred stocks resemble bonds in a key way: The dividend they pay every quarter is fixed — similar to a bond's interest payment — unlike a common share dividend, which often fluctuates each quarter.&#160;</p><p>Although that flow isn't contractually guaranteed the way it is with bonds, companies generally feel obligated to give precedence to paying preferred dividends over common dividends.</p><h2><strong>How preferred stocks work</strong></h2><p>Getting to be ahead of common stockholders in the dividend line is only one of preferred shares' unique features.</p><p>Here are the basics of how preffered stocks work:</p><ul><li><strong>Preferred stock dividends are usually a lot higher than common-stock dividends</strong>, and their jumbo size is essentially the whole reason people buy them. The dividends, which are paid quarterly, are expressed as a percentage of their issued value (called \"par\"); this percentage is often called their coupon rate. For instance, a preferred stock issued at a par of $50 with a coupon of 6.75% will pay out about $0.84 a quarter, or $3.35 annually.</li><li><strong>Most preferreds are callable</strong>, meaning that a company may decide to force investors to sell their shares back to them at the prevailing market price, plus some sort of premium.&#160;</li><li><strong>Many preferreds are also convertible</strong>, meaning that a share can be changed into common stock. For instance, a stock's prospectus may say that one share of preferred can be changed into five shares of common stock once a certain date has passed. (In some cases, a company can even force preferred owners to make that conversion.)</li></ul><h2><strong>What the \"preferred\" in preferred stock means</strong></h2><p>The price of a preferred share can fluctuate in daily trading, just like its common share counterpart. It can, and does, reflect what's happening to the company. But because most preferreds are callable, the upside is more limited, and their share price stays pretty close to par value, as noted earlier. The par value is usually akin to what a preferred share would buy in common stock.</p><p>So what's the preferred thing worth? It really only comes into play when the company's in trouble: Preferred shareholders always get their dividends before common shareholders if a company has serious financial problems <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-liquidity\">affecting cash flow</a>, or otherwise decides to suspend dividends. Creditors, employees, bondholders, and a few other groups are still ahead of them in the getting-paid line, though.&#160;</p><p>Of course, most companies make a strong effort to pay dividends through hell and high water. Suspending preferred share dividends is a pretty drastic step. One nice thing, though: when companies are able and willing to begin paying dividends again, they are obliged to start paying them on preferred shares before they can start paying them on common stock.</p><h2><strong>Who buys preferred stock?</strong></h2><p>Loading up on common stock <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/why-invest-in-stocks\">makes sense</a> for lots of different kinds of investors, but the market for preferreds is more limited.&#160;</p><p>Most preferred stock is bought by institutions and pension funds. They love the higher dividends and are better equipped to assess the risks, including the fact that preferreds are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-are-liquid-assets\">less liquid </a>(easily sold) than common stock. Institutions also get special tax advantages from preferreds in some cases.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Because the dividends are taxed as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/how-much-is-capital-gains-tax%20asset%20and%20your%20income%20level\">capital gains</a> if they are held longer, they may also make sense for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investment-income-assets\">income-oriented individual investors </a>who'd otherwise buy bonds. That's because bond payments are interest, which is always taxed as normal income. In contrast, stock dividends qualify for a lower tax rate if you own them as a longer-term investment (longer than a year, usually).&#160;</p><p>Still, for most investors, preferreds' downsides outweigh their potential. They may pay out more than bonds do, but those dividends aren't guaranteed. And if they won't ever appreciate much in value the way common stock does, since a company would simply call them before that happens.&#160;</p><h2>The financial takeaway</h2><p>Preferreds aren't called that because they're so classy. They're preferred because their dividends have to be paid before those that would go to the common stockholders.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Preferred stock pays higher dividends than common stock, but its share price will never appreciate the way common stock might. So, the upside's more limited.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Preferreds are best for institutional investors or for more sophisticated individuals, who want them in their portfolio for tax reasons or for some other particular goal. Despite their advantages, they have several aspects to keep track of. Most individual investors don't need the hybrid features that preferreds are known for.</p><h2>Related Coverage in&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">Investing</a>:</h2><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-an-etn\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"15\" data-analytics-module=\"\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">ETNs combine a bond's reliability with a stock's profitability. Here's how they work, and how to weigh the risks and rewards</a></h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-an-index-fund\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"featured_post\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">What is an index fund? A low-cost, low-risk way to invest in the stock market</a></h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-buy-treasury-bonds\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"9\" data-analytics-module=\"\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">How to buy treasury bonds, one of the safest ways to invest for income</a></h3><h3><a you're starting from scratch</a></h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-volatility\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"7\" top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><div id=\"ProductCard_5fad8d77977c4353197660a7\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5fad8d77977c4353197660a7&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><h2>Education and personal development</h2><p>For the book lover in your life, check out Oprah's recommendations for meaningful reads.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5fa0851f851d5a631f7f9039\" style=\"position:relative; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><h2>Health and fitness</h2><p>Nobody <em>needs</em> a $2,000 <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/mirror-review\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">workout mirror</a>, but we've heard that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/1500-dollar-mirror-streams-workout-classes-review-2018-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">anyone who has</a> it loves it.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5fad522ee155cf1cfc230547\" style=\"position:relative; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><h2>Pets&#160;</h2><p>Treat the pooch in your life with a gift for yourself — because who is dressing up dogs in hoodies <em>really</em> for?&#160;</p><p>Editor's note: Both of the Pride and Groom sets were out of stock at the time of publishing, but you can bookmark the links below and check back in when it gets closer to the holidays. Many items from Oprah's Favorite Things go in an out of stock between the time the list is released and the beginning of the holidays.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5fad5b08f348c31ce30365b4\" id=\"ProductCard_5fac033ad67e12656955b8a0\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/GWhZT61aAyk\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 16 Nov 2020 21:51:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fb2e8471c741f0019aca1bc?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"1a39486b5f9e8775e2060b85ff8c613b","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn3@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-39-03-577_6ca3070f688e8cff.webp","destWidth":1666,"destHeight":1249,"sourceBytes":156450,"destBytes":156450,"author":"skaplan@businessinsider.com (Sally Kaplan)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb2e833402d49001924f3ec?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn76@2020_4/2020/11/17/05-38-50-255_1c2610b82e0e6b8f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn44@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-39-00-474_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=GWhZT61aAyk:uH2WDUy8NXY:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn32@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-39-02-308_6c90f5f28d6a49b9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=GWhZT61aAyk:uH2WDUy8NXY:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn63@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-51-544_bc29704d95cfebd5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-53-238_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=GWhZT61aAyk:uH2WDUy8NXY:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn79@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-48-228_f18b9bab3e821c13.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/GWhZT61aAyk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn12@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-39-00-910_a821bbf31b74c60c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605591522181},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"19 signs that you're a narcissist and don't even know it","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/signs-you-are-a-narcissist-2015-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9b12fd6f5b31001172445d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"selfie makeup\" height=\"2649\" width=\"3532\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hrytsiv Oleksandr/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>Narcissists often believe that they're better-looking than others, enjoy taking advantage of and belittling other people, and usually engage in a series of romantic relationships.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>We put together a list of 19 typical behaviors of narcissists, based on research and expert opinion.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>This list isn't intended to be diagnostic, but it can give you a good idea of whether you or someone you know might have narcissistic traits.</strong></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories.</a></li>\n</ul><p>Narcissism is a distinct personality disorder, which according to<a href=\"https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/conditions/narcissistic-personality-disorder\"> Psychology Today</a>, is characterized by \"grandiosity, a lack of empathy for other people, and a need for admiration.\"</p><p>The traits that make narcissists so difficult to hang out with or date — like a willingness to control people and a ruthlessness in getting their needs met — also happen to make them<a href=\"http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/peps.12072/abstract\"> effective at rising up the ranks</a>. Narcissists only make up about<a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/national/health-science/narcissists-are-everywhere--but-they-may-not-be-the-people-you-think-they-are/2016/10/07/175d79ee-867d-11e6-a3ef-f35afb41797f_story.html\"> 1% of the population</a>, but when you think of the hundreds of people you know, chances are there are may be a few narcissists mixed in.&#160;</p><p>To help you figure out if you, your family member, or perhaps your boss is a narcissist, we combed through the psychology literature looking for patterns of narcissistic behavior. We also spoke with Joseph Burgo, PhD, a psychologist and the author of<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/The-Narcissist-You-Know-All-About-Me/dp/1476785686\"> \"The Narcissist You Know.\"</a></p><p>Here are 19 common signs of narcissism, and how to identify them.</p><p><em>This is an update of an article originally written by Vivian Giang, with additional contributions by Drake Baer.&#160;</em></p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\t1. You're a bad sport\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d1f8cfaa17d6c0e5a5fa3a2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"andy murray tennis sport\" height=\"2460\" width=\"3280\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dennis Grombkowski/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Burgo&#160;says some narcissists are bullies &#8212; and one of their most troublesome traits is their tendency to be a sore loser&#160;<em>and</em>&#160;a sore winner.</p><p>For example, when they lose in a sports match, narcissistic people might try to humiliate the referee. When they win, they might gloat excessively or act abusively to the losing party.</p>\n\t2. You constantly feel under appreciated\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cdc101c021b4c76947c4df5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"waitress unhappy\" height=\"1800\" width=\"2400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zero Creatives/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The kind of people that Burgo calls \"grandiose\" narcissists always hold a grievance against the world.</p><p>Those with narcissistic behavior will typically feel entitled to something better and think they're not getting the recognition they deserve from others.</p>\n\t3. If you're not grandiose, then you're introverted, hypersensitive, defensive, and anxious\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cd9ce09021b4c35be608ad2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"coworker meeting\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hero Images/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Psychologists talk about the \"<a href=\"http://scottbarrykaufman.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/Two-faces-of-Narcissism.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">two faces of narcissism</a>.\" On one end there's the hyper-aggressive, super-loud type. But there's a softer form of narcissism, too. It's called \"covert narcissism,\" which is denoted by introversion, hypersensitivity, defensiveness, and anxiety.</p><p>\"Both shades of narcissism shared a common core of conceit, arrogance, and the tendency to give in to one's own needs and disregard others,\" Scientific American <a href=\"http://blogs.scientificamerican.com/beautiful-minds/2013/08/26/23-signs-youre-secretly-a-narcissist-masquerading-as-a-sensitive-introvert/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reports</a>.</p>\n\t4. You think everyone else is stupid\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d1f983ba17d6c00e043ad76?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elon Musk, the founder of SpaceX, at a press conference following the successful launch of the rocket company&#39;s Crew Dragon spaceship, which was designed for NASA astronauts, on March 2, 2019. elon musk spacex crew dragon nasa spaceship demo 1 mission expression surprised wtf frowning thinking 2019 03 02T092850Z_1799206996_RC11F8939950_RTRMADP_3_SPACE SPACEX.JPG\" height=\"1636\" width=\"2181\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.reutersconnect.com/all?id=tag%3Areuters.com%2C2019%3Anewsml_KCN1QI553&#38;share=true\" target=\"_blank\">Reuters</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Many&#160;narcissists are know-it-alls, and have a hard time getting along with coworkers and friends because they refuse to believe they could possibly be wrong about anything.</p><p>Burgo has observed that these narcissists walk around with a marked sense of superiority to others and have a \"my way or the highway\" approach to decision-making.</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\t5. You really like to swear at people\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dddb429fd9db22dfa790c38?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Furious boss yelling at colleagues\" height=\"3744\" width=\"4992\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Wavebreakmedia/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Psychologists Nicholas Holtzman and Michael Strube from Washington University in St. Louis <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">found</a> in a study that subjects who scored higher in narcissism are argumentative and curse more than their modest counterparts.</p><p>They also tend to use more sexually explicit language.</p>\n\t6. You are self-righteous\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d0102e66fc92056c16c92c6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"conversation coworkers\" height=\"2700\" width=\"3600\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">fizkes/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Narcissists often believe their views are inherently superior to other people's perspectives. But what they truly value is the attention they receive for holding those views.</p><p>For example, Burgo said, a person with narcissism might believe he has a closer connection to God &#8212; but it's more important to him that other people acknowledge this connection and admire his deep sense of spirituality.</p>\n\t7. You feel justified in being mean to people\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cb8d679c3a7c123b957e3c8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"annoying coworker\" height=\"4643\" width=\"6191\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">BartekSzewczyk/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>\"Vindictive\" narcissists generally know vengeful or antisocial behavior isn't acceptable. But they feel OK about acting that way because they constantly feel they've been wronged, Burgo said.</p><p>What's more, they often take offense where it's not intended, meaning they're constantly hearing people say, \"That's not what I meant!\"</p>\n\t8. You enjoy leading others and telling them what to do\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/58adcacf54905755008b629e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"speech presentation audience lecture\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Matej Kastelic/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Narcissists <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">typically enjoy leadership positions</a> since they are able to dominate others and fulfill their need for constant positive reinforcement.</p>\n\t9. You are likely young and male, and maybe an entertainer\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5617d08cbd86ef195c8b57ea?format=jpeg\" alt=\"kanye west\" height=\"2456\" width=\"3275\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kevork Djansezian/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>\"A narcissist monk would not be good, but to be Kanye West and a narcissist is fantastic,\" <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said</a> University of Western Sydney psychologist Peter Jonason, an expert on social psychology.&#160;</p><p>After 34,653 face-to-face interviews, psychologist Frederick Stinson <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">found</a> that men tend to be more narcissistic than women across their lifespans.</p><p>Narcissism is believed to peak during adolescence and decline with age.</p>\n\t10. You hate having to feel emotions\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5617f47c9dd7cc1a008c094a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"pepper robot\" height=\"2258\" width=\"3011\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Yuya Shino/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The \"very fact of having a feeling in the presence of another person suggests you can be touched emotionally by friends, family, partners, and even the occasional tragedy or failure,\"&#160;<a href=\"http://www.huffingtonpost.com/dr-craig-malkin/narcissists_b_3331293.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">says Harvard Medical School psychologist Craig Malkin</a>.</p><p>That's why narcissists abhor them.</p><p>Feeling an emotion \"challenges their sense of perfect autonomy,\" he continues. \"To admit to a feeling of any kind suggests they can be affected by someone or something outside of them.\"</p><p>As a result, narcissists tend to change the topic of conversation when feelings come up &#8212; especially their own.&#160;</p>\n\t11. You're more attractive than other people — or at least you think you are\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d1f9f86a17d6c028e3d5105?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Narcissist\" height=\"800\" width=\"1067\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jacob Lund/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Narcissists are generally rated as more stylish and physically attractive, <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\">according to a study</a> conducted by Simine Vazire, a&#160;psychologist at Washington University.</p><p>However, this isn't always the case. According to a <a href=\"https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0191886908001967\">2008 study</a>, narcissists rated themselves highly in both looks and intelligence, but when they took IQ tests, the results were average. When their peers were asked to rate their narcissist friends on looks, the results were lower than what the narcissists gave themselves.</p>\n\t12. Instead of listening, you just wait to speak\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5617d778bd86efed5b8b584d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"cover ears\" height=\"890\" width=\"1187\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/ Issei Kato</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Anita Vangelisti, a psychologist at the University of Texas in Austin, <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">found</a> that narcissists typically prefer to keep the conversation centered on&#160;themselves, \"making exaggerated hand movements, talking loudly, and showing disinterest by 'glazing over' when others speak.\"</p>\n\t13. You are a serial romantic\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5335880f69beddad3675da9e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"couple kissing\" height=\"2204\" width=\"2939\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Christian Hartmann/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Burgo also identifies a group of narcissists he calls \"seductive.\"</p><p>These people with narcissistic traits fall in and out of love quickly and easily, often with people they don't know very well. They think their partner is absolutely perfect &#8212; a complement to their own perfection &#8212; until reality sets in, when they realize their partner is flawed and end the relationship.</p>\n\t14. You cheat in relationships, and usually get dumped after dating for about four months\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a213da13dbef4a7748b8f1e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"cheating couple\" height=\"1334\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">wavebreakmedia/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Psychologists Joshua Foster at the University of South Alabama and W. Keith Campbell at the University of Georgia <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">found</a>&#160;that narcissists are more likely to cheat once they think their partners are committed.</p><p>They also seem to get a rush out of convincing others to engage in promiscuous sexual acts that they normally do not participate in.</p><p>Through his research, Campbell also <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">found</a> that the four-month mark &#8212; the apparent satisfaction peak in any dating relationship &#8212; is typically how long it takes for someone dating a narcissist to see their true colors.</p>\n\t15. You put some people on pedestals\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cbf3045b14bf4236f4eb0e2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"statue of liberty\" height=\"1374\" width=\"1832\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Malkin&#160;<a href=\"http://www.huffingtonpost.com/dr-craig-malkin/narcissists_b_3331293.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">says</a>&#160;the logic goes like this: \"If I find someone perfect to be close to, maybe some of their perfection will rub off on me, and I'll become perfect by association.\"</p><p>With that ideal in mind, narcissists cozy up to people they find perfect &#8212; be it a colleague or a crush &#8212; and then get really disappointed when that person isn't as impeccable as they imagined.</p><p>For a narcissist, everything has to be perfect.</p>\n\t16. You like to put other people down\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5caf5f1353c7111db6236ad5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"talking to your boss\" height=\"4912\" width=\"6549\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Westend61/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Narcissistic people intentionally put down others in order to maintain a high positive image of themselves.</p><p>\"Seeking admiration is like a drug for narcissists,\" <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said</a> Mitja D. Back, a psychologist at Johannes Gutenberg University in Mainz, Germany. \"In the long run, it becomes difficult because others won't applaud them, so they always have to search for new acquaintances from whom they get the next fix.\"</p><p>This also explains why narcissists typically maintain only weak relationships.</p>\n\t17. Your parents both ignored and adored you\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cf52b8411e20506e27a8ed3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"parenting\" height=\"1385\" width=\"1847\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">shapecharge/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/0146167205279907\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/10.1177/0146167205279907&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1562440607409000&#38;usg=AFQjCNG0meXbaKQ20sOxmf-ezMczI2mbUA\">Research suggests</a>&#160;a combination of parental rejection and excessive admiration is more strongly linked to adult&#160;narcissism&#160;than if one childhood experience consistently existed without the other.</p><p>The inconsistency and whiplash of the parents' attitude toward their children will eventually cause a \"deep craving for admiration\" and lead the narcissist to lead a life searching for fleeting ego boosts, <a href=\"https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/articles/201107/how-spot-narcissist\">Psychology Today reports</a>.</p>\n\t18. You choose your friends to look cool or take advantage of people\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ad87f130b0b9240008b4879?format=jpeg\" alt=\"girls selfie friends\" height=\"853\" width=\"1138\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.shutterstock.com/image-photo/multi-ethnic-friends-having-fun-city-199956071?src=4pwDaqgG-qsE4KFZwoHOCA-1-42\" target=\"_blank\">Peter Bernik / Shutterstock</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Narcissistic men and women have <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">different ways of choosing friends</a>.&#160;</p><p>Women choose male friends with high social status so they can feel a sense of worthiness. Guys choose bros who can \"wingman\" for them when they're trying to pick up girls, according to <a href=\"http://www.psychologytoday.com/articles/201106/how-spot-narcissist\">Psychology Today</a>.</p>\n\t19. You always have to be in control\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d0ed4cee3ecba5d873022d3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"kim jong un\" height=\"1117\" width=\"1489\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In this undated photo provided on Sunday, June 23, 2019, by the North Korean government, North Korean leader Kim Jong Un reads a letter from U.S. President Donald Trump.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Korean Central News Agency/Associated Press</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Just as narcissists hate to talk about their feelings, \"they can't stand to be at the mercy of other people's preferences,\" Malkin says. \"It reminds them that they aren't invulnerable or completely independent &#8212; that, in fact, they might have to&#160;<em>ask</em> for what they want &#8212; and even worse, people may not feel like meeting the request.\"</p><p>This is why they can be controlling without getting angry. In the case of romantic relationships, narcissists control people with disapproving glances, calls to change plans, and chronic lateness.&#160;This allows narcissists to undermine other people's ability to make choices. By doing that, narcissists maintain their sense of total autonomy &#8212; which they so desperately need.</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb322a5fb29831da9652ea8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 945288850\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption>\n   Jose Bello was arrested by ICE after reading a poem condemning deportations. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">John Moore/Getty Images</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>Jose Bello was arrested by Immigration and Customs Enforcement in 2019 after a public reading of a poem, \"Dear America,\" condemning the Trump administration's immigration crackdown.</li> \n <li>The American Civil Liberties Union alleges that he was targeted in retaliation for his speech, violating the First Amendment.</li> \n <li>On Tuesday, Bello's lawyers will argue before a US federal court that he was targeted for his activism.</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>Jose Bello came to the United States when he was three years old — and fewer than two days after speaking out against the Trump administration's immigration policies, the college student was arrested at his home in Southern California and slated for deportation.</p>\n<p>On Tuesday, Bello's lawyers will argue before a US federal court that he was targeted for his activism and that his detention violates the right to free speech.</p>\n<p>In 2019, Bello attended a meeting of the Kern County Board of Supervisors, where during a public comment session he read a poem, \"Dear America,\" defending the rights of immigrants and condemning the federal government's crackdown on the foreign-born.</p>\n<iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/AYIt-euHKuY\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n<p>\"We know who you are and what you're about,\" one agent with Immigration and Customs Enforcement told Bello the morning he was arrested, according to the American Civil Liberties Union. ICE set bail at $50,000 — more than twice Bello's income as a farm worker.</p>\n<p>In court, ICE has argued that it has a right to detain Bello, regardless of what actually sparked his arrest, because the then-22-year-old had a prior conviction for driving under the influence. And that argument has, thus far, prevailed in the US justice system, where agents of the state have been granted de facto immunity for suspected retaliatory arrests provided there is \"probable cause\" for the detention.</p>\n<p>Tuesday's hearing will be before the US Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit. In a <a href=\"https://www.aclusocal.org/sites/default/files/brf.9cir.18_opening_brief.pdf\">brief filed with the court</a>, attorneys with the American Civil Liberties Union say the court should reverse an earlier judgment upholding the arrest and reject \"ICE's dangerous position as anathema to the First Amendment protection against retaliation for speech.\"</p>\n<p>ICE did not immediately respond to a request for comment.</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip?
