src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2f9a7402d49001924f45e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Biden-president-elect-wilmington\" height=\"2664\" width=\"3996\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President-elect Joe Biden won the 2020 US presidential election with 306 electoral votes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Andrew Harnik</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>In the 2020 US presidential election, President-elect Joe Biden earned 306 electoral votes to 232 electoral votes for President Donald Trump.</li>\n<li>This year, Biden flipped five states and one congressional district that Trump won 2016, giving him the majority in both the Electoral College and the popular vote.</li>\n<li>Biden won the traditionally Republican states of Arizona and Georgia, neither of which had voted for a Democratic presidential nominee since the 1990s.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>On November 14, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-election-results\">the final puzzle piece</a> of the 2020 presidential map was set.</p><p>Once President-elect Joe Biden <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/joe-biden-wins-georgia-democratic-party-south-presidential-election-2020-11\">was declared the winner in Georgia</a>, based on a projection by Decision Desk HQ and Insider, the final Electoral College tally in the presidential election stood at 306 electoral votes for Biden and 232 electoral votes for President Donald Trump. Biden is well over the 270 electoral vote threshold needed to secure the presidency.</p><p>As of November 17, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-election-results\">Biden leads in the national popular vote</a> by a 51% to 47% margin, or by 4 percentage points. So far, Biden has earned 78,729,579 votes, compared to Trump's 73,126,938 votes, with outstanding ballots still being counted in several states, including California and New York.&#160;</p><p>Biden's raw vote lead is currently just under 6 million votes.</p><p>While the 2016 presidential map reflects Democratic dominance on the East and West coasts and Republican strength across the interior of the country, the 2020 map shows how Biden made significant inroads in every region of the country.</p><p>Here are some key differences between the 2016 presidential race between Trump and former Secretary of State Hillary Clinton and this year's election between Trump and Biden:</p><h3>The 2020 Electoral College total is the inverse of the 2016 results</h3><p>Biden's 306 electoral votes and Trump's 232 electoral votes are the exact inverse of the 2016 presidential election, when Trump received 306 electoral votes to 232 electoral votes for Clinton.</p><p>The final 2016 presidential map reflects 304 electoral votes for Trump and 227 electoral votes for Clinton because both candidates lost two and five electoral votes, respectively, due to faithless electors.</p><p>Faithless electors are members of the Electoral College <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/electoral-college-donald-trump-president-official-2016-12\">who vote against the state or district's popular vote winner</a>. For Clinton, there were four faithless electors in Washington State and one faithless elector in Hawaii, while Trump had two faithless electors in Texas. Before 2016, the last time that there were any faithless electors was the 2004 presidential election between then-President George W. Bush and Sen. John Kerry of Massachusetts.</p><p>This year, members of the Electoral College, who have already been picked by the states and Washington DC, will meet on December 14 to cast their votes for the winner of each state or district.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2fa641c741f0019aca246?format=jpeg\" alt=\"2016 vs 2020 pres maps\" height=\"1280\" width=\"890\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shayanne Gal/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3>Biden flipped 5 states that Trump won in 2016</h3><p>Throughout the presidential campaign, Biden focused on restoring the \"blue wall,\" the collection of states that had voted for every Democratic presidential nominee from 1992 to 2012, while also competing in the Sun Belt, which included the key states of Arizona, Florida, Georgia, and Texas.</p><p>Biden was successful in not only <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/joe-biden-sweeps-pennsylvania-michigan-wisconsin-battleground-states-election-2020-11\">flipping Pennsylvania, Michigan, and Wisconsin</a>, but he also carried Arizona (49.4%-49.1%) and Georgia (49.5%-49.2%). However, he came up short in Florida (48%-51%) and Texas (46%-52%).</p><p>Pennsylvania, with its 20 electoral votes, was a critical battleground for both Biden and Trump. The president narrowly won Pennsylvania in 2016, but Biden carried the state this year by performing strongly in Philadelphia and its suburbs, along with Pittsburgh and the northeastern region of the state.</p><p>Michigan (16 electoral votes) and Wisconsin (10 electoral votes) were key Midwestern prizes that were part of Biden's calculus for winning the White House.&#160;</p><p>The wins in Arizona (11 electoral votes) and Georgia (16 electoral votes) reflected the party's growing strength in fast-growing areas of the country that are rapidly diversifying and are home to large numbers of suburban voters, who were a critical part of the Democratic coalition in 2020.</p><p>Lastly, Biden won the 2nd congressional district of Nebraska, anchored by Omaha, the state's largest city. Since the state allocates its electoral votes by Congressional districts, the president-elect earned one electoral vote, while Trump won the remaining four electoral votes.</p><p>The key difference from 2016? Clinton didn't win any of these states — had she just won Pennsylvania, Michigan, and Wisconsin, then she would have headed to the White House instead of Trump.</p><h3>Biden and Trump each won 25 states</h3><p>In the 2020 presidential election, Biden won 25 states, along with Washington DC and Nebraska's 2nd congressional district. Trump also won 25 states, along with Maine's 2nd congressional district.</p><p>In 2016, Trump won 30 states and Maine's 2nd congressional district, while Clinton only won 20 states and Washington, DC.</p><p>Despite Trump winning the same number of states as Biden this year, he still fell well short in the Electoral College. Biden carried most of the country's largest states by incredibly wide margins, which propelled his national vote lead.</p><p>In this election, Trump became only <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-join-10-presidents-who-didnt-win-reelection-2020-10\">the 11th president in US history</a> to lose reelection. The last president who failed to win a second term was George H.W. Bush in 1992, who was defeated by then-Gov. Bill Clinton of Arkansas.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-vs-2016-electoral-college-maps-trump-biden-clinton-president-2020-11'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=qU5Iq1C3ecA:RVvXv78dH3A:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/qU5Iq1C3ecA\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 16 Nov 2020 23:07:06 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fb03336402d49001924f002?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"a8d1d4f3a089464f0c280090a904d389","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn97@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-38-47-130_1653ee670ba04cd9.webp","destWidth":1250,"destHeight":937,"sourceBytes":67000,"destBytes":67000,"author":"insider@insider.com (John L. documents publicly available on Monday, providing the most detailed look yet at the company's inner financial workings.</p>\n<p>Airbnb reported a third quarter profit of $219.3 million on $1.3 billion in revenue, up from a second-quarter net loss of $575.6 million on $334.8 million in revenue as the company saw bookings rebound slightly after plummeting this summer amid the pandemic.</p>\n<p>Airbnb's third quarter revenue dropped nearly 18% compared to the same quarter last year — better than third quarter revenues reported by top competitors like Booking.com (<a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/ix?doc=/Archives/edgar/data/1075531/000107553120000073/bkng-20200930.htm#i11e35b6bb5094c5fa20a52a07c651185_22\">down 48%</a>) and Expedia (<a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/ix?doc=/Archives/edgar/data/1324424/000132442420000077/expe-20200930.htm\">down 58%</a>) as well as Airbnb's first two quarters of 2020.</p>\n<p>But Airbnb's profitable third quarter came amid severe cost-cutting measures and revealed exactly how hard the pandemic has devastated its business.&nbsp;</p>\n<p>For the first nine months of the year, Airbnb's prospectus revealed a revenue of $2.5 billion, down 32% from $3.7 billion during the same period last year, while its losses grew to $696.9 million from $322.8 million. Airbnb reported annual revenue of $4.8 billion in 2019.</p>\n<p>Airbnb, like the rest of the industry, has been hit hard by the massive decline in travel this year. So far in 2020, travelers have booked 146.9 million nights or experiences through Airbnb, down 41% from the same period last year. Airbnb said it experienced the sharpest decline during the the second quarter, with bookings down 67% year-over-year, while business bounced back slightly in the third quarter with a decline of 28% from the same quarterly period last year.</p>\n<p>However, Airbnb said it projects higher year-over-year declines in bookings and cancellations during the fourth quarter than in the third quarter as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-200000-new-coronavirus-cases-2-days-50-states-rising-2020-11?r=ts-sub\">COVID-19 cases surge again</a> this winter.</p>\n<p>Airbnb cited the pandemic among a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ipo-risk-factors-pandemic-declining-revenue-not-profitable-2020-11#2-revenue-growth-is-slowing-and-the-company-expects-it-to-continue-to-slow-going-forward-2\">long list of risk factors</a> that could adversely impact its financial outlook, including slowing revenue growth, an uncertain regulatory landscape as more local governments pass laws aimed at curbing or taxing short-term rentals, nearly $2 billion in debt, and lingering questions about its profitability.</p>\n<p>The company plans to list its shares on the Nasdaq under the ticker symbol \"ABNB,\" and will offer an unspecified number of Class A common stock, but the filing revealed the company has a complicated share structure that includes four classes: Class A, Class B, Class C, and Class H.</p>\n<p><strong>Read more:</strong><em> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnbs-founders-agree-to-keep-each-other-on-the-board-2020-11\">Airbnb's three founders have put two unusual twists on their efforts to retain control after their company goes public</a></em></p>\n<p>Morgan Stanley and Goldman Sachs are the lead banks for the offering, through which Airbnb said it's expecting to raise $1 billion — a likely placeholder number. The startup is reportedly looking to raise around $3 billion, according to <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/16/business/dealbook/clayton-sec-stepping-down.html\">The New York Times' Dealbook</a>.</p>\n<p>Airbnb was last privately valued at $18 billion, according to <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/airbnb-paying-more-than-10-interest-on-1-billion-financing-announced-monday-11586297484\">The Wall Street Journal</a>. It <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-confidentially-filed-for-an-initial-public-offering-2020-8?r=ts-sub\">confidentially filed to go public</a> in September and enters a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-tech-ipos-in-2020-including-airbnb-palantir-and-snowflake-2020-8?r=ts-sub\">red-hot IPO market</a> in what will likely be one of the largest offerings this year.</p>\n<p>The company's decision ended speculation over how the pandemic would affect its IPO timeline, and it will likely alleviate some of the pressure the company has faced for years from employees whose stock options were <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/20/technology/airbnb-employees-ipo-payouts.html\">set to start expiring</a> this month if the company didn't go public.</p>\n<h2>Pandemic perils</h2>\n<p>Airbnb has had a long and at times bumpy <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-charts-graphics-show-evolution-impact-hotels-travel-comparison-industry-2020-1?r=ts-sub\">road to its IPO</a>, particularly during the past several months as the coronavirus pandemic wreaked havoc on the travel industry. Monday's filing comes amid record new COVID-19 cases in the US.&nbsp;</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ceo-brian-chesky-pandemic-challenges-resiliency-ipo-interview-2020-9?r=ts-sub\">Airbnb's Brian Chesky says what it was like to watch his company's revenue plunge 80% in eight weeks and how he decided to go public anyway in exclusive interview</a></em></p>\n<p>When travel restrictions hit in early March, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ceo-brian-chesky-pandemic-challenges-resiliency-ipo-interview-2020-9?r=ts-sub\">Airbnb's revenue plummeted 80%</a>, CEO Brian Chesky told Business Insider in September. Bookings in Beijing dropped as much as 96%, according to AirDNA, raising existential questions for the travel giant and forcing it to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-halts-hiring-marketing-report-2020-3?r=ts-sub\">freeze all marketing spending</a> and nearly all hiring.</p>\n<p>Already <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-could-out-of-cash-in-year-due-to-coronavirus-2020-4?r=ts-sub\">burning through its cash reserves</a>, Airbnb <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-paying-10-percent-interest-debt-valuation-cut-18-billion-2020-4?r=ts-sub\">raised $1 billion in debt and equity financing</a> from Silver Lake and Sixth Street Partners at a steep interest rate of more than 10% and a valuation of $18 billion — down nearly 50% from its previous valuation of $31 billion, The Journal reported. A week later, the company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-raising-1-billion-debt-second-funding-deal-two-weeks-2020-4?r=ts-sub\">raised an additional $1 billion in debt</a> from the two banks and other investors at a 7.5% interest rate.</p>\n<p>As of May, Airbnb still expected its revenue for the year to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnbs-revenue-falls-more-than-half-brian-chesky-coronavirus-layoffs-2020-5?r=ts-sub\">less than half of its 2019 earnings</a>, forcing it to take even more drastic measures. Airbnb <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-layoffs-cutting-1900-jobs-25-percent-staff-coronavirus-2020-5?r=ts-sub\">laid off 1,900 employees</a> — 25% of its staff — and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-laid-off-most-of-its-contract-workers-over-zoom-2020-4?r=airbnb-lp\">nearly all its contractors</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-hosts-criticized-260-million-assistance-plan-2020-4?r=ts-sub\">faced backlash from hosts</a> over its early COVID-19 cancellation policies, and&nbsp;paused its investments in ambitious projects around luxury accommodations and producing travel content in order to focus on its core business.</p>\n<p>Airbnb's business recovered a bit during the third quarter, partly due to Chesky's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ceo-brian-chesky-predicts-future-of-travel-digital-nomad-2020-5?r=ts-sub\">bets on post-pandemic travel trends</a>, which have <a href=\"https://skift.com/2020/08/14/airbnb-and-vrbo-significantly-outperformed-the-hotel-industry-but-for-how-long/\">so far paid off</a>. He predicted people would flock to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/rural-airbnbs-thriving-as-americans-flee-cities-to-escape-coronavirus-2020-3?r=ts-sub\">rural and local destinations</a> over international tourist traps and big cities, travel more for leisure while using screens for work (instead of the other way around), and prefer private spaces over crowded ones like chain hotels.</p>\n<p>Those gains also came as domestic travel and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-q3-gdp-record-growth-economic-reopening-recession-coronavirus-pandemic-2020-10?r=ts-sub\">the US economy bounced back</a> more generally, and as Airbnb cut total expenses to just over $3 billion for the first nine months of this year, down 22% from $3.9 billion during the same period last year.</p>\n<h2>Other questions remain</h2>\n<p>While going public may allow Airbnb's early investors and employees to breathe a sigh of relief, the company still has significant challenges ahead and will be under even greater scrutiny as a public firm.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-top-five-challenges-investors-focus-prepares-public-2020-2020-1?r=ts-sub\">As Airbnb prepares for an IPO amid the pandemic, here are 6 of the company's challenges that are worrying investors</a></em></p>\n<p>Investors will likely focus heavily on the company's path to profitability. Airbnb said it had a few profitable quarters before the pandemic hit — the second and third quarters of 2018, as well as the third quarter of 2019 — but acknowledged that it has \"incurred net losses in each year since inception, and we may not be able to achieve profitability.\"</p>\n<p>Airbnb said it incurred net losses of $70 million, $16.9 million, and $674.3 million in 2017, 2018, and 2019, respectively, and expects to incur an annual loss again in 2020.</p>\n<p>It's also not clear how well the company will weather the coronavirus pandemic, especially as cases <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-200000-new-coronavirus-cases-2-days-50-states-rising-2020-11\">surge ahead of the winter months</a>. While Airbnb has recovered more quickly than hotels so far, according to a study from <a href=\"https://skift.com/2020/08/14/airbnb-and-vrbo-significantly-outperformed-the-hotel-industry-but-for-how-long/\">AirDNA and STR</a>, part of that could be attributable to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/which-is-safer-airbnb-hotels-coronavirus\">coronavirus travel trends</a> that aren't guaranteed to continue after the virus recedes.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Are you an Airbnb insider with information to share? </em></strong><em>Contact this reporter via encrypted messaging app Signal at (+1) 503-319-3213 using a nonwork device, email at </em><a href=\"mailto:tsonnemaker@businessinsider.com\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"8f3fc2da35afe135f3d85f805623d8fc\"><em>tsonnemaker@businessinsider.com</em></a><em>, or Twitter DM at @TylerSonnemaker. target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Our Place</a> (modern dinnerware and drinkware).&#160;</li><li><a data-stringify-link=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/insider-picks\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Sign up for Insider Reviews' weekly newsletter for more buying advice and great deals.</a></li></ul><p>Cooking is not a skill that we simply enter the world knowing. We learn how to cook from a variety of sources — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-cookbook-for-beginners\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cookbooks</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cozymeal-cooking-class-review\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">classes</a>, parents, friends, cooking shows — but it can still be complex and confusing.</p><p>That's how most of us initially shop for and use cookware, too: bumbling around, trying to make sense of different materials and the purposes they serve, and collecting tools from parents and roommates that have seen countless kitchens before our own. Sure, you can throw out your old pots and pans and start from scratch, but if you want high-quality, well-constructed cookware and dinnerware, you often have to pay up first, spending hundreds of dollars on name brands.&#160;</p><p>You're not alone in these struggles, and in just the past few years, new companies have emerged to lend you a helping hand in the kitchen, with many offering products for half the price of traditional brands like Le Creuset, All-Clad, and Staub. These startups understand that the joys of cooking and eating become even sweeter when your kitchenware lasts a lifetime but doesn't take a lifetime to pay off.&#160;</p><h2>If you're looking to upgrade your kitchen tools and cookware without breaking the bank, check out our 12 favorite direct-to-consumer kitchen companies.&#160;</h2>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tMade In: Cookware used by both home cooks and top professionals\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e42f9952dae5c09620eca75?format=jpeg\" alt=\"online kitchen startups made in 2\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Made In</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&#38;u=1088116&#38;m=74508&#38;urllink=madeincookware.com%2F%3Futm_source%3Dshareasale%26utm_campaign%3D1088116%26utm_medium%3Daffiliate%26utm_term%3D1108190%26sscid%3Db1k4_hxont\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Shop cookware at Made In here</a>&#160;</h3><p><strong>Product range:&#160;</strong>Stainless clad pots and pans, carbon steel pans, knives, and accessories (spoons, blocks, etc.)&#160;</p><p><strong>Background: </strong>Childhood pals Chip Malt and Jake Kalick, whose Boston-based family business, Harbour Food Service Equipment, designs and outfits commercial kitchens, wanted to create a one-stop-shop for exceptional, ethically-made cookware. The pair partnered with family-owned manufacturers in the US, France, and Italy on a line of products that meet professional chefs' exacting standards at price points that are accessible to home cooks.&#160;</p><p>The brand's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/kitchen-startups-made-in-material-tap-expert-advisors-tom-colicchio-alison-roman\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">investors and advisors</a> include \"Top Chef\" judge Tom Colicchio and Alinea Group cofounders Grant Achatz and Nick Kokonas, and Made In can be found in renowned restaurants like New York City's Le Bernardin. Another fun way it leverages its connections to the restaurant biz is through <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&#38;u=1088116&#38;m=74508&#38;urllink=madeincookware.com%2Fcollections%2Fchef-collaboration-series\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Chef Collaborations</a>, which includes things like the<a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&#38;u=1088116&#38;m=74508&#38;urllink=madeincookware.com%2Fproducts%2Ffamily-meal-vol-1%3Fvariant%3D31463605796943\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">\"Family Meal Vol. 1\" book of recipes</a> from 15 different chefs, and the Contra kit, a previous project with NYC's Michelin-starred Contra that bundled ingredients along with a carbon steel frying pan and a mother of pearl tasting spoon.&#160;</p><p>Celebrity ties aside, Made In often uses <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/successful-products-inspired-by-customers-demands\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">customer feedback</a> to influence product design and release decisions, like the introduction of their highly lauded <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&#38;u=1088116&#38;m=74508&#38;urllink=madeincookware.com%2Fproducts%2Fblue-carbon-steel-wok\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">carbon steel wok</a>.&#160;</p><p><strong>Materials and construction: </strong>While Made In's original claim to fame was its focus on American manufacturing, it now also enlists the help of experienced factories in France and Italy to craft its carbon steel pans and steel knives. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/made-in-cookware-overview\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">We've tested much of the company's cookware</a> and found the pieces to be durable and well-made.&#160;</p><p><strong>Other things to know about Made In:</strong></p><ul><li>Free shipping on orders over $50&#160;</li><li>45-day return policy</li><li>Lifetime warranty&#160;</li><li><a rel=\"noopener nofollow\">Financing</a> available</li></ul><p><strong>What you should buy:</strong></p><div id=\"ProductCard_5e41c5d03b62b743c474fab8\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: Basic kitchen tools that don't skimp on style\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e42f7233b62b7046a3dada6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"online kitchen startups material kitchen\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Material Kitchen/Instagram</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=1128903&#38;u=1088116&#38;m=76897&#38;urllink=https%3A%2F%2Fmaterialkitchen%2Ecom%2F&#38;afftrack=\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\">Shop kitchen tools and cookware at Material here</a></h3><p><strong>Product range:&#160;</strong>Kitchen tools, copper core pans, knives, and accessories (boards, wood oil, etc.)</p><p><strong>Background: </strong>Material's founders Eunice Byun and David Nguyen hated their cluttered kitchens, which were filled with hand-me-downs, poor-quality tools, unnecessary accessories, and unsophisticated color palettes.<strong style=\"color: #ff0000;\">&#160;</strong>So they set out to make the kitchen gear they wished they had: simple, thoughtfully-designed, long-lasting products at affordable prices.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/material-kitchen-fundemental-set-review-2018-3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">We've used NASA","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/astronauts-attach-spacex-crew-dragon-spaceship-international-space-station-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb35743dc6df8228d11bfa4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"crew-1 docking crew dragon iss spacex nasa\" height=\"1069\" width=\"1425\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Crew Dragon spaceship sitting docked to the International Space Station as NASA astronaut Kate Rubins carries out hatch-opening procedures, November 16, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">NASA TV</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>SpaceX on Sunday <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-launches-rocket-mission-nasa-astronauts-crew-1-dragon-spaceship-2020-11\">launched</a> its first operational mission into orbit for NASA with four astronauts on board.</li>\n<li>On Monday night, the astronauts caught up to International Space Station and docked.</li>\n<li>The mission, named Crew-1, calls for the astronauts to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-crew-1-mission-timeline-nasa-astronaut-launch-2020-11\">spend the next six months at the ISS</a> &#8212;&#160;the longest human spaceflight ever launched from US soil.</li>\n<li>The commercial mission represents a major opportunity for NASA to boost the amount of scientific research it can perform on the ISS, and sets the stage for future flights of private astronauts.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>On Monday night, four astronauts arrived at the International Space Station inside SpaceX's Crew Dragon spaceship, teeing up what could be a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-crew-1-mission-timeline-nasa-astronaut-launch-2020-11\">record-breaking stay</a> in orbit.</p><p>The NASA-funded commercial mission, called Crew-1, marks the first \"operational\" human spaceflight by SpaceX, the rocket company Elon Musk founded in 2002. It follows the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/photos-spacex-nasa-astronaut-mission-to-space-station-2020-8\">Demo-2 mission</a>, SpaceX's first launch of people, which lifted off in May and returned to Earth in August.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/crew-1-astronaut-bios-spacex-nasa-mission-2020-11\">astronauts of Crew-1</a> — Victor Glover, Mike Hopkins, and Shannon Walker of NASA, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-starship-dearmoon-crew-japanese-astronaut-soichi-noguchi-yusaku-maezawa-2020-9\">Soichi Noguchi</a> of the Japan Aerospace Exploration agency — lifted off from Kennedy Space Center in Florida on Sunday night atop a Falcon 9 rocket. The astronauts spent most of the night settling into <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astronauts-name-spacex-spaceship-resilience-ahead-of-nasa-launch-2020-9\">Resilience</a>, as they named their space capsule, while helping SpaceX troubleshoot propellant and cabin heaters issues.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2e777402d49001924f3e6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"spacex nasa crew dragon spaceship launchpad arm falcon9 rocket crew1 mission launch florida spacex 2020 11 15 50607431543_a47f52da70_o edit\" height=\"1892\" width=\"2524\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Falcon 9 rocket built by SpaceX lifts off Launch Complex 39-A carrying four astronauts aboard the Crew Dragon &#34;Resilience&#34; spaceship on November 15, 2020, at Kennedy Space Center in Cape Canaveral, Florida.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.flickr.com/photos/nasahqphoto/50607431543/in/album-72157716809424867/\" target=\"_blank\">Joel Kowsky/NASA</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>On Monday, the vehicle fired its thrusters several times to catch the ISS, beginning a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/watch-live-spacex-crew-dragon-docking-to-international-space-station-2020-11\">rendezvous with the football-field-size laboratory</a> around 9 p.m. ET. Resilience spent an hour maneuvering about 400 meters in front of the facility, then another hour carefully — and automatically — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-spaceship-docking-video-game-simulator-international-space-station-2020-5\">inching forward</a> while the astronauts looked over flight data.</p><p>\"They won't have to push any buttons or fire any thrusters, Dragon is doing this all on its own — it's completely autonomous,\" Leah Cheshier, a NASA communications specialist, said during a live broadcast on Monday night.</p><p>The ship gently bumped into and engaged a temporary locking mechanism at 11:01 p.m. ET, softly anchoring the astronauts to their new home.</p><p>\"Resilience, SpaceX. Docking sequence is complete. Welcome to the ISS,\" a SpaceX mission controller told the crew as grapple hooks tightly secured their vehicle onto a port around 11:13 p.m. ET.</p><p>\"Excellent job, right down the center,\" responded Hopkins, the mission's commander. \"SpaceX and NASA, congratulations: This is a new era of operational flights to the International Space Station from the Florida coast.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb34b58d0c5f826d4268d52?format=jpeg\" alt=\"spacex crew1 mission docking crew dragon resilience astronauts international space station nasatv 00001\" height=\"413\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Astronauts monitor SpaceX&#39;s Crew Dragon Resilience as the spaceship autonomously docks to the International Space Station on November 16, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3hK540tMmvw\" target=\"_blank\">NASA/SpaceX</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Before Crew-1 can join the ISS crew — astronaut Kate Rubins and cosmonauts Sergey Ryzhikov and Sergey Kud-Sverchkov, who launched in October — several steps remain. The crews have to pressurize an adapter with air, check for leaks, then open all the hatches. NASA expects the big moment to happen around 1:10 a.m. ET on Tuesday.</p><p>Resilience and its passengers aim to spend the next six months in space. Assuming all goes well, Crew-1 is slated to become the longest human spaceflight ever launched from US soil, beating a record set more than 45 years ago.</p><p>By expanding the ISS crew, those aboard won't have to spend so much of their time on maintenance, which will enable NASA to conduct more scientific research than before.</p><h2>A commercial boost to the space station after 20 years in orbit</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/582b7a25ba6eb61b008b456d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"international space station iss nasa\" height=\"1530\" width=\"2400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The International Space Station (ISS).\n<p class=\"copyright\">NASA</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Since the US retired its space shuttles in 2011, NASA has had to buy astronauts seats on Russia's Soyuz spaceships to get to and from the ISS — a facility that's been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-space-station-is-about-celebrate-20-years-human-presence-2020-10\">inhabited by humans continuously for 20 years</a>.&#160;</p><p>To help close the gap, NASA launched the Commercial Crew Program a decade ago: a competition to spur private companies to develop new spaceships. The roughly $8 billion program led SpaceX to develop Crew Dragon, and Boeing to develop its CST-100 Starliner (which may fly its first crew in late 2021).</p><p>NASA funded the Crew Dragon's creation with about $3 billion, and engineers at SpaceX designed, built, and tested it to exacting government requirements. Agency heads <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-certifies-spacex-fly-astronauts-crew-dragon-spaceship-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"467745c2cbe2a6dbaafb8905c6143790\">finally certified the system</a> for regular flight last week — in large part because of the success of the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-safely-splashes-down-nasa-astronauts-crew-dragon-demo2-mission-2020-8\">Demo-2 flight</a>, which carried NASA astronauts Bob Behnken and Doug Hurley to and from the space station.</p><p>\"This is the culmination of years of work and effort from a lot of people, and a lot of time, and we have built I think what I would call is one of the safest ... launch vehicles and spacecraft ever,\" Benji Reed, SpaceX's director of crew mission management, said during a press briefing before Crew-1's launch.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb286dc402d49001924f13a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"crew 1 nasa jaxa astronauts wave waving launch practice kennedy space center cape canaveral florida november 2020 NHQ202011120002_orig\" height=\"1292\" width=\"1723\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Astronauts (from left) Shannon Walker, Victor Glover, and Mike Hopkins of NASA, and Soichi Noguchi of JAXA, wear SpaceX spacesuits on their way to Launch Complex 39A during a Nov. 12 dress rehearsal ahead of the Crew-1 mission launch from Kennedy Space Center in Florida.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://images.nasa.gov/details-NHQ202011120002\" target=\"_blank\">Joel Kowsky/NASA</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Crew-1 is the first of six round trips that NASA has purchased from SpaceX, and it formally kicks off <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-boeing-nasa-commercial-crew-program-launch-astronauts-2020-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"85740095c562d61232e48d88940d75a1\">an era of commercial spaceflight</a>. The vehicle isn't limited to professional astronauts: Private astronauts may also fly to space in the coming years.</p><p>For example, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tom-cruise-travel-elon-musks-spacex-rocket-film-space-movie-2020-5\">Tom Cruise</a> and director Doug Liman are planning to launch to the ISS in 2021 aboard a Crew Dragon spaceship to film a movie. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-first-space-reality-show-send-1-lucky-winner-iss-2020-9\">Space Hero</a>, a reality TV show, is also angling to fly a contestant to the facility in 2023. A company called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/axiom-space-private-astronaut-mission-agreement-2020-3\">Axiom Space</a> plans to contract SpaceX for the tickets.</p><p>The most important thing to NASA, though, is expanding the crew of the space station. The ISS offers an unparalleled zero-gravity environment in which to perform research that can't be conducted on Earth. However, science is hard to get done when only a few crew members are on the ISS, since they're often preoccupied with regular cleaning and maintenance. Occasionally, their time also gets taken up <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astronauts-cosmonauts-found-space-station-leak-using-tea-leaves-2020-10\">hunting for leaks</a> and fixing toilets.</p><p>Now, with SpaceX looking to maintain a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-will-have-crew-ship-in-orbit-14-months-2020-10\">continuous presence in orbit</a> with Crew Dragon, the space station can be fully staffed — and NASA can make good on its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/space-station-trump-plan-problems-astronaut-risk-2018-5\">$100 billion investment</a> in the facility.</p><p>Crew-1 aims to&#160;<a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/mission_pages/station/research/news/spacex-crew-1-science-iss\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">power a variety of research</a>, including studying how the body responds to eating certain foods in microgravity and spaceflight's <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/mission_pages/station/research/experiments/explorer/Investigation.html?#id=8350\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">effects on astronaut brains</a>. The crew will also experiment with <a href=\"https://ncats.nih.gov/tissuechip/projects/space\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tissue chips</a>, <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/mission_pages/station/research/experiments/explorer/Investigation.html?#id=7793\">plant growing</a>, and even <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/mission_pages/station/research/experiments/explorer/Investigation.html?#id=7514\">part of a new spacesuit</a> designed for the moon and Mars.</p><p>\"We are ready for the six months of work that is waiting for us on board the International Space Station, and we are ready for the return,\" Hopkins said during a pre-flight briefing.</p><h2>Watch the ongoing Crew-1 mission live on NASA TV:</h2><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/21X5lGlDOfg\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe><p><em>This is a developing sensitivity, build enamel, whiten your teeth, and freshen your breath, all while helping promote a healthy mouth.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>Our top pick, <a To get the most out of your daily brushing, it's smart to use the correct type of toothpaste. Most types are made to solve specific problems inside your mouth, including everything from eliminating sensitivity and rebuilding enamel to whitening teeth and freshening your breath.</p><p>Although some companies' claims sound dubious, many&#160;kinds of toothpaste actually work as advertised. After all, to get on the ADA's list, companies have to scientifically demonstrate the safety and efficacy levels of its toothpaste.</p><p>We've researched and tested many tubes of toothpaste to find the best currently available. We updated prices, links, and formatting. We also removed our top pick for the best all-natural toothpaste since it has unfortunately been discontinued, as well as our top pick for the best with charcoal since it is currently out of stock and studies have shown charcoal toothpastes may actually lead to tooth decay.&#160;&#160;</em></p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tThe best toothpaste overall\n\t<figure>\n\t<img breath nicely</p><p><strong>Cons: </strong>Build quality of tubes is questionable, taste isn't for everyone</p><p>Even though the <a href=\"https://goto.walmart.com/c/196318/565706/9383?veh=aff&#38;sourceid=imp_000011112222333344&#38;u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.walmart.com%2Fip%2FSensodyne-Pronamel-Gentle-Whitening-Fluoride-Toothpaste-to-Strengthen-and-Protect-Enamel-4-Ounce-Twinpack-2-tubes-of-4oz%2F17248395\" As it strengthens your enamel, it also whitens gently.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://goto.walmart.com/c/196318/565706/9383?veh=aff&#38;sourceid=imp_000011112222333344&#38;u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.walmart.com%2Fip%2FSensodyne-Pronamel-Gentle-Whitening-Fluoride-Toothpaste-to-Strengthen-and-Protect-Enamel-4-Ounce-Twinpack-2-tubes-of-4oz%2F17248395\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow\">Pronamel Gentle Whitening Toothpaste</a>&#160;won't irritate gums or the lining of the mouth, either, because it doesn't contain sodium laurel sulfates. complications.&#160;The toothpaste is ADA approved, so these claims are actually validated to some extent with scientific testing.</p><p>Colgate claims that this toothpaste will keep your breath fresh charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbnb Founders, Chief Product Officer Joe Gebbia, CTO Nathan Blecharczyk and CEO Brian Chesky speak onstage during the &#34;Introducing Trips&#34; Reveal at Airbnb Open LA on November 17, 2016 in Los Angeles, California.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Windle/Getty Images for Airbnb</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Airbnb's founders said many likely didn't expect the company to go public as the COVID-19 pandemic battered its business by 80% and stalled its IPO, which was reported to kick off in March.</li>\n<li>The rental startup's business has plunged as travel bookings declined due to the coronavirus crisis &#8212; the founders said the firm has issued over $1 billion refunds.</li>\n<li>Airbnb filed for an initial public offering Friday.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Airbnb's founders said people likely didn't expect the rental startup to go public this year as the COVID-19 pandemic battered its business by 80% and resulted in the company issuing more than $1 billion in refunds.</p><p>Airbnb was reportedly due to kick off the IPO process in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-may-push-ipo-back-to-2021-because-of-coronavirus-2020-3\">March and April</a>, which coincided with the first devastating months of the pandemic. Reports then surfaced that its IPO could be stalled until 2021. It confidentially filed to go public in September, but in its <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1559720/000119312520294801/d81668ds1.htm\">S-1</a> filed Monday, Airbnb officially unveiled the 12-year-old <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-files-s1-public-ipo-paperwork-revenue-losses-covid-19-2020-11\">company's IPO documents.</a></p><p>\"When borders closed and travel stopped, our business declined by nearly 80%,\" Airbnb founders Brian Chesky, Nate Blecharczyk, and Joe Gabbia wrote in a letter that accompanied the S-1. \"We had to put our IPO on hold, and I don't think many people expected us to go public this year. I know some people questioned if we'd make it at all. What has transpired since then has been our most defining period since we started Airbnb.\"</p><p>The founders closed the letter, saying: \"In the depths of this crisis, some people asked, 'Is this the end of Airbnb?' It was not the end of Airbnb. In fact, it was just the beginning. It's still early. We invite you to come on this journey with us.\"</p><p>The S-1 filing revealed the company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-files-s1-public-ipo-paperwork-revenue-losses-covid-19-2020-11\">suffered a net loss</a> of $696.9 million during the first three quarters of 2020 but reported $2.52 billion in revenue. The pandemic has slammed Airbnb's business, forcing the startup to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnbs-layoffs-will-likely-save-company-less-than-255-million-2020-5\">lay off</a> hundreds of employees and battering its booking revenue by 72% in Q2 amid pandemic-driven travel restrictions.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-quirky-airbnb-hosts-owners-keep-business-up-safe-travel-2020-10?r=kc-sub\">Owners of some of the quirkiest Airbnbs in the US share how their businesses have taken off and pivoted to accommodate cautious travelers looking for an escape</a></em></p><p>The company has bounced back slightly by adapting to changes in customer travel trends, like an uptick in rural and local bookings. But it still has its work cut out for it, especially as health experts predict coronavirus cases to surge in the upcoming winter.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a height=\"762\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can delete a Reddit post on mobile or on a computer in a few simple steps.\n<p class=\"copyright\">SOPA Images/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>You can delete a Reddit post that you aren't proud of or that is simply irrelevant now by heading to your profile settings.</li>\n<li>You can delete posts using both the Reddit website and the mobile app, but the process will slightly vary for each.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Perhaps your <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/reddit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Reddit</a> post in /r/neoliberal is getting downvoted en masse by the foot soldiers of the /r/swoletariat community.</p><p>Perhaps you realized your post unintentionally violated a subreddit's rules and you want to avoid getting perma-banned.&#160;</p><p>Perhaps you simply \"posted cringe,\" to put it in Generation Z-speak.</p><p>Whatever the reason, no one is perfect, and neither are your Reddit&#160;posts.</p><p>If you decide it's prudent to purge one of your Reddit&#160;musings from the web, here's how, on both the mobile and desktop platforms.&#160;</p><h2>How to delete a Reddit post using a computer<strong>&#160;</strong></h2><p><strong>1.&#160;</strong>Open Reddit in your web browser of choice on your computer, and sign in by clicking \"Log in\" in the top right corner.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8cb04e73d0c8523f5e2a65?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to delete Reddit post\" height=\"800\" width=\"1280\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Signing into Reddit, on Mozilla&#39;s Firefox browser.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>2. </strong>An icon will be in the top right corner that you may or may not have customized. Click the arrow next to the icon for a dropdown menu.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8cb0ba29d6d95a5603b7f5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to delete Reddit post\" height=\"760\" width=\"1280\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Click the small arrow.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>3.&#160;</strong>Select \"My Profile,\" and from the options at the top select \"Posts.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8cb08d29d6d95a30274536?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to delete  Reddit post\" height=\"760\" width=\"1280\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The &#34;My Profile&#34; page, where your posts and comments will be sorted by most recent.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4.&#160;</strong>All your posts will be listed, sorted by most recent. Find the post you want to delete. Then, find the ellipses icon, next to \"Edit Post.\"&#160;</p><p><strong>5.&#160;</strong>Click it, and select \"Delete.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8cb10c8427e94e4d70e0e6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to delete Reddit post\" height=\"800\" width=\"1280\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Your post history, automatically sorted by most recent to oldest.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>6.&#160;</strong>A pop-up will warn you that deleting a post can't be undone. Click \"Delete Post\" to finalize.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8cb14db3b09257f77440a5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to delete Reddit post\" height=\"800\" width=\"1280\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Be cautious about posts you want to delete — they can&#39;t be resurrected once they&#39;re gone.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>How to delete a Reddit post using a mobile device</h2><p><strong>1.&#160;</strong>Open the Reddit app on your <a href=\"https://apple.sjv.io/c/196318/435031/7613?subId1=biipg_091817_best-iphone&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-iphone%2Fiphone-11e-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPhone</a> or <a href=\"https://www.walmart.com/ip/Samsung-Galaxy-S10-G973-128GB-Unlocked-GSM-LTE-Phone-with-Triple-12MP-12MP-16MP-Rear-Camera-Prism-Black/104597743\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Android</a>. If you haven't downloaded it already, you can find it as \"Reddit\" in your device's app store.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.&#160;</strong>Tap your profile icon to log in, if you haven't already.&#160;</p><p><strong>3.&#160;</strong>Navigate to \"My profile\" by tapping your user icon in the top-left corner, and then tap \"My profile\" under your username.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8cb190c02320509341041b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to delete Reddit post\" height=\"2436\" width=\"1125\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>If you haven&#39;t yet customized your avatar, you&#39;ll see Reddit&#39;s iconic laughing robot as a placeholder.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4. </strong>You'll automatically be taken to your posts. Scroll to the post you'd like to delete.</p><p><strong>5.&#160;</strong>Tap the ellipses \"...\" symbol on the right side, just above the post's title.</p><p><strong>6.&#160;</strong>Click \"Delete post,\" indicated by the trashcan icon, and click \"Delete\" when you're prompted by Reddit.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8cb1e915ea4b47a32f516a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to delete Reddit post\" height=\"2436\" width=\"1125\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Other than minor aesthetic differences, the Reddit for iPhone and Android apps are almost identical in how you use them.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><div id=\"ProductCard_5d8e19fb2e22af18f40d281d\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"How to change a playlist's name on Spotify using the desktop or mobile app","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-change-playlist-name-on-spotify","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2f5d31c741f0019aca22e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"spotify app headphones\" height=\"1500\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can edit the name of your Spotify playlist on the mobile and desktop apps.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Trutschel/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>You can change a playlist's name on both the Spotify desktop and mobile apps, but you will need to be the owner of the playlist.&#160;</strong></li>\n<li>To change a playlist's name on the Spotify mobile app, first access it from the \"Your Library\" tab before selecting \"Edit Playlist\" from the three-dotted Settings menu.&#160;</li>\n<li>You can change a playlist name on the Spotify desktop app by selecting \"Edit Details\" from the three-dotted Settings menu directly under a playlist's title.&#160;</li>\n<li>If you don't see the \"Edit Playlist\" or \"Edit Details\" options, try refreshing the app &#8212; you don't have editing access for that playlist.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Playlist titles can be a form of self-expression, but sometimes inspiration just doesn't strike and you end up with something like, \"Happy playlist\" or even just a string of random letters.</p><p>If you use Spotify, you don't have to keep those placeholder titles. You can easily edit the names of your playlists. However, you can only edit playlists that you own.</p><p>Here's how to edit a Spotify playlist's name, using either the desktop version for Mac and PCs or the mobile app for iPhone and Android devices.</p><h2><strong>How to change a playlist name on Spotify using the desktop app</strong></h2><p><strong>1. </strong>Open Spotify on your Mac or PC and log into your account, if necessary.</p><p><strong>2. </strong>Open the playlist that you want to change the name of.</p><p><strong>3. </strong>Click the three dots under the name of the playlist and select \"Edit Details.\"</p><ul><li><strong>Note:</strong> If you don't see this option, you don't have editing access for that playlist.</li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e4daec3a27fc566782901c7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to Change Playlist Name on Spotify   1\" height=\"1408\" width=\"2366\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can also click on the playlist&#39;s title or cover art.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Devon Delfino/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4. </strong>Add your new playlist name in the \"Name\" field, in addition to a description if desired.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e4daedf043895654450ffb3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to Change Playlist Name on Spotify   2\" height=\"1416\" width=\"2368\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can add both a name and description.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Devon Delfino/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>5.</strong> Click \"Save.\"</p><h2><strong>How to change a playlist name on Spotify using the mobile app</strong></h2><p><strong>1. </strong>Open the Spotify app on your iPhone or Android device.</p><p><strong>2. </strong>Tap the \"Your Library\" tab in the bottom toolbar, and tap the playlist you want to edit the name of.</p><p><strong>3. </strong>Tap the three dots in the top-right corner of the screen and select \"Edit\" or \"Edit playlist.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e4daf16a27fc566cf4763d4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to Change Playlist Name on Spotify   4\" height=\"2220\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Select the &#34;Edit&#34; option.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Devon Delfino/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4. </strong>Tap the title at the top and change it however you like, and then select \"Save.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e4daf3004389565e0486554?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to Change Playlist Name on Spotify   5\" height=\"2220\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Edit the playlist&#39;s name.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Devon Delfino/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2><strong>Related class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>You can easily switch profiles on Hulu while watching on your smart TV, mobile device, or computer.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Hulu profiles let you customize your viewing experience by remembering your watch history, suggesting new programs, and letting you pick up shows where you left off.<br ></strong></li>\n<li><strong>You can have up to six separate profiles on one Hulu account, and switch between them at any time.</strong></li>\n<li>This story is a part of Business Insider's&#160;<a and Tricks</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Does your significant other love police procedurals and shows about cupcake bakeries, while you prefer sitcoms, rom coms, and horror movies?&#160;</p><p>Then it sounds like you two have very different taste in programming, and rather odd taste at that. But that's OK, with your very own <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/hulu\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hulu</a> profile you can carve out your own customized viewing experience.&#160;</p><p>Your Hulu profile gives you quick access to shows or movies in progress, episodes of your favorite series, and helps you find new material you just might love.</p><p>If you opened Hulu up only to find a cop show or baking program staring at you, then you'll need to switch profiles to get back to the lighthearted comedies and terrifying films you love.&#160;</p><p>Here's how to switch Hulu profiles on your phone, computer, and TV.</p><h2>How to switch profiles on Hulu using your computer</h2><p><strong>1.&#160;</strong>Log into your Hulu account on your <a href=\"http://apple.sjv.io/c/196318/435031/7613?subId1=biipgf_122917_best-macbooks&u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-pro-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener href=\"https://go.redirectingat.com/?id=35871X943606&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.walmart.com%2Fip%2FHDMI-RAM-3-7GHz-Windows-130-4GB-Notebook-Bluetooth-Display-AMD-Wi-Fi-Home-Upto-10-Lenovo-Dual-Core-SSD-Card-DVDRW-IdeaPad-256GB-Reader-HD-15-6-A9-9425%2F7105106980698\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">PC</a>.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.&#160;</strong>Hover your cursor over your profile in the top-right corner of the screen.</p><p><strong>3.&#160;</strong>Click on the profile you wish to switch in the dropdown menu.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e84e76514f18f7fd255c5db?format=jpeg\" alt=\"how to switch hulu profiles\" height=\"790\" width=\"1439\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Select your profile from the list.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Isabella Paoletto/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>How to switch profiles on Hulu using your mobile device&#160;<em>&#160;</em></h2><p><strong>1.&#160;</strong>To switch Hulu profiles on your iPhone or Android, tap the account icon in the bottom-right of your screen in the app.&#160;<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e84bc9e2d654f14c620714d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to switch profiles on Hulu\" height=\"1792\" width=\"828\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tap “Account.”\n<p class=\"copyright\">Isabella Paoletto/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>2.&#160;</strong>Then, tap on your current profile at the top of your screen and select the profile you wish to switch to from the menu.&#160;<em>&#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; &#160; height=\"1792\" width=\"828\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Select the profile name.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Isabella Paoletto/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>How to switch profiles on Hulu using your smart TV</h2><p><strong>1. </strong>Use your smart TV's remote or connected device, navigate to your account icon.</p><p><strong>2.</strong> Select \"Profiles\" from the menu that appears.</p><p><strong>3. </strong>Select your preferred profile.&#160;</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5dd83bd0fd9db23c6131fb54\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"Georgia's top election official says Lindsey Graham pressured him to throw out all mail ballots cast in certain counties","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/lindsey-graham-pressured-georgia-top-election-official-to-toss-ballots-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb302601c741f0019aca267?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brad Raffensperger \" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Georgia Secretary of State Brad Raffensperger speaks during a news conference on Wednesday, Nov. 11, 2020, in Atlanta. Georgia election officials have announced an audit of presidential election results that will trigger a full hand recount.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Brynn Anderson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Georgia's Republican Secretary of State Brad Raffensperger told The Washington Post that GOP Senator Lindsey Graham pressured him to throw out entire counties' worth of ballots for signature issues.&#160;</li>\n<li>Raffensperger is facing attacks on his credibility and the integrity of Georgia's election from fellow Republicans after President Trump lost the state in the Electoral College.&#160;</li>\n<li>Raffensperger said that Graham asked if the signature verification process was subject to political bias and asked if Raffensperger could disqualify ballots.&#160;</li>\n<li>Graham denied Raffensperger's account of the conversation and said the notion he pressured Raffensperger to get ballots thrown out was \"ridiculous.\"</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Georgia's Republican Secretary of State Brad Raffensperger is facing death threats, public attacks from fellow Republicans, and even pressure to throw out all the mail ballots cast in entire counties, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/brad-raffensperger-georgia-vote/2020/11/16/6b6cb2f4-283e-11eb-8fa2-06e7cbb145c0_story.html\">he told the Washington Post in an interview published on Monday.</a></p><p>Raffensperger, who was elected in 2018 to succeed now-Governor Brian Kemp, was criticized in June by some Democrats over long lines to vote and other issues in the state's primary.</p><p>But now, with Republicans <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-election-results\">losing Georgia in the presidential race for the first time since 1992</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-senate-runoff-elections-jon-ossoff-david-perdue-warnock-loeffler-2020-11\">having to fight to defend both the state's US Senate seats in runoffs</a>, the state's chief election official says he's undergoing a barrage of attacks on his credibility and the integrity of Georgia's election from prominent elected officials from within his own party.</p><p>He told The Post that Senator Lindsey Graham of South Carolina, the chairman of the Senate Judiciary Committee and a powerful figure in the GOP, directly asked if he could disqualify thousands of mail ballots for mismatched signatures.&#160;</p><p>Raffensperger said Graham questioned whether ballots with mismatched signatures were wrongly accepted because of election workers holding political bias towards Democrats, and asked if Raffensperger himself could throw out all the mail ballots cast in counties with higher than average rates of ballots being flagged for signature issues.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/brad-raffensperger-georgia-vote/2020/11/16/6b6cb2f4-283e-11eb-8fa2-06e7cbb145c0_story.html\">As The Post noted,</a> Raffensperger does not have the authority to categorically disqualify scores of ballots in entire counties. An effort to do so would require legal action in court, and for a judge to rule that the ballots were illegally cast or fraudulent.&#160;</p><p>Talking to reporters on Capitol Hill, Graham disputed Raffensperger's account of the conversation, telling The National Journal's Zach Cohen that Raffensperger \"did a good job\" explaining the signature verification process and called the notion that he pressured Raffensperger to get ballots disqualified \"ridiculous.\"&#160;</p><p>\"It seems to me that Georgia has some protections that maybe other states don't have, where you go into the portal to get your ballot. But I thought it was a good conversation. I'm surprised to hear he characterized it that way,\" Graham said, according to Cohen.</p><p>Georgia is one of around 30 states that uses signature matching to verify the authenticity of mail ballots. In that process, election officials compare the signature on the outer envelope with the voters' most recent signature on file. A mismatched signature is not necessarily indicative of fraud, as peoples' signatures sometimes change over time, and Georgia <a href=\"https://www.11alive.com/article/news/politics/elections/2020-election-cure-absentee-ballot-georgia/85-c7e1858e-4a44-4c41-9a82-694a21c39e13\">has an established cure process for voters to fix problems with their signature.&#160;</a></p><p>The intra-party battle began heating up shortly after Election Day when Republicans Senators David Perdue and Kelly Loeffler, who are now advancing to January runoffs, <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/11/09/loeffler-perdue-georgia-secretary-state-resign-435484\">called on Raffensperger to resign from office,</a> claiming without presenting any evidence that he \"failed to deliver honest and transparent elections.\"</p><p>There is no evidence of any widespread fraud or irregularities in Georgia. The state <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/ap-explains-georgia-audit-or-recount-9adf1d0ed50f8788572b4f7e0f04027e\">is currently conducting a comprehensive risk-limiting audit</a> of the presidential race that is expected to confirm that President-elect Joe Biden decisively won the state in the Electoral College.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/11/09/politics/georgia-2020-election-kelly-loeffler-david-perdue-brad-raffensperger/index.html\">In a blunt response to Loeffler and Perdue,</a> Raffensperger rejected their demand that he should step down and defended the integrity of the election. \"As a Republican, I am concerned about Republicans keeping the U.S. Senate. I recommend that Senators Loeffler and Perdue start focusing on that,\" he wrote.</p><p>Rep. Doug Collins, who challenged Loeffler in the special jungle election to replace Sen. Johnny Isakson, has also attacked Raffensperger's credibility.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/brad-raffensperger-georgia-vote/2020/11/16/6b6cb2f4-283e-11eb-8fa2-06e7cbb145c0_story.html\">In his interview with The Post</a>, Raffenspeger called Collins a \"liar\" and a \"charlatan.\"&#160;</p><p>Raffensperger and Kemp have both been criticized on Twitter <a href=\"https://www.ajc.com/news/as-trump-rages-georgia-recount-continues/VIUTVDNHPJBELNGNSRGY5QKFOM/\">by President Donald Trump</a>, who accused them of being RINOs (Republicans In Name Only), <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/ap-fact-check-donald-trump-georgia-elections-voter-registration-40bb602e6f0facf8eecc331e83ab36e0\">falsely suggested that a consent decree</a> that Georgia entered into to standardize its signature verification procedures is \"unconstitutional,\" and <a href=\"https://factcheck.thedispatch.com/p/explaining-the-conspiracy-theories?token=eyJ1c2VyX2lkIjo2NzI5NTksInBvc3RfaWQiOjE4ODc2ODU2LCJfIjoiem1JamgiLCJpYXQiOjE2MDU0NjYzMzIsImV4cCI6MTYwNTQ2OTkzMiwiaXNzIjoicHViLTIyMDYzIiwic3ViIjoicG9zdC1yZWFjdGlvbiJ9.u2fRaw2pKX5GRyl5BlNFLQkcPdA8bhKsWRNWluBjdU0\">spread unfounded conspiracies attacking Dominion Voting Systems</a>, the vendor that provides Georgia's ballot marking device voting machines.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/FaqwKKrgDSM\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 17 Nov (Grace Panetta)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb302601c741f0019aca267?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn67@2020_2/2020/11/17/05-38-56-872_412ceeba9e470126.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn44@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-39-00-474_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=FaqwKKrgDSM:FGWaMWNttag:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn76@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-58-297_aa59b477a46aeee0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=FaqwKKrgDSM:FGWaMWNttag:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn72@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-39-01-809_b26b889002b70470.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/05-38-53-238_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=FaqwKKrgDSM:FGWaMWNttag:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn59@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-38-52-981_3141b84ee20fece0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/FaqwKKrgDSM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn59@2020_1/2020/11/17/05-38-58-122_3387229e621fccdd.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605591522180},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 13:38:42","title":"How 5-year-old startup Shopee is leading e-commerce growth in Southeast Asia","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/shopees-digital-inclusion-strategy-e-commerce-growth-in-southeast-asia-2020-11","description":"<div class=\"content-header\"><p><a href=\"https://businessinsider.com/tb/the-people-transforming-business-in-2020-9\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://media.tbistatic.com/bistudios/_00/dev/ING/story_banners/ING_edit_banner.png?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Transforming Business\" height=\"\" width=\"\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p></div><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fad664cdf90d0001837819a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1158922709 min\" height=\"3332\" width=\"4443\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo Illustration by Rafael Henrique/SOPA Images/LightRocket via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>The value of Southeast Asia's e-commerce sector is estimated at $38 billion and is on track to surpass $150 billion by 2025.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Founded in 2015, Singapore-based Shopee is the region's leading e-commerce platform by monthly active users</strong></li>\n<li><strong>The company has built its business on a mobile-first strategy that reflects high mobile internet usage in the region</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Shopee is investing in digital inclusion to help new and existing merchants recover from the pandemic</strong></li>\n<li>Because of his work, Business Insider named Shopee's COO, Terence Pang, to our annual list of the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tb/the-list-of-300-people-transforming-business-in-asia-2020-9\">10 leaders transforming retail in Asia.</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tb/the-people-transforming-business-in-2020-9\"><strong>Visit Business Insider's Transforming Business homepage for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>While much of the retail sector in Southeast Asia was hit hard due to lockdowns and other restrictions in the early months of the COVID-19 pandemic, e-commerce continues to grow at speed, with consumers and merchants alike increasingly turning to online platforms.&#160;</p><p>According to Google Trends, Thailand saw a 63% increase in e-commerce search interest in May compared to the same time in 2019. Malaysia and Vietnam also experienced positive levels of interest, with increases of 32% and 13% respectively.</p><p>This growth is nothing new for the region – the pandemic is merely accelerating an existing trend. A joint report from Google, Temasek and Bain and Company estimated that the eCommerce sector in SEA was worth over $38 billion in 2019, up from $5.5 billion in 2015. The report forecasts that e-commerce value in the region will surpass $100 billion by 2025.&#160;</p><p>Riding this boom is Shopee, the leading e-commerce site in the region measured by average monthly active users. Headed by CEO Chris Feng alongside COO Terence Pang, Shopee launched in Singapore in 2015 as a social-first, mobile-centric marketplace. Here are four key strategic factors driving Shopee's journey from ambitious startup to a regional retail powerhouse.</p><h2><strong>Mobile first. Always.</strong></h2><p>Southeast Asians are the most engaged mobile Internet users in the world. According to the Google, Temasek, and Bain and Company report, there are 360 million Internet users in the region and 90% of them connect to the Internet primarily through their mobile phones.&#160;</p><p>From the beginning, Shopee saw mobile as an emerging trend and the way forward for e-commerce in the region. It immediately focused on optimizing user experience and engagement through mobile. The company says online shopping must evolve to fit the needs of younger users in particular who grew up communicating, collaborating, and entertaining themselves on mobile devices. Shopee's mobile-first approach allows it to take advantage of the expected continued growth in mobile subscriber penetration.</p><p>Shopee says that over 95% of orders on the platform are now made on mobile. Responding to this demand, Shopee offers an end-to-end online shopping experience directly on the mobile app. Buyers are able to browse products, order, make payment, and track the status of deliveries. At the same time, sellers are able to use the app to take a photo, create listings, monitor shop performance, receive payments and track deliveries through integrated logistics and payment tools.&#160;</p><h2><strong>Taking a hyper-local approach</strong></h2><p>Southeast Asia is a region and not a single market. Each country has different e-commerce characteristics and challenges, and the demographics of consumers also differ from market to market. With this in mind, Shopee takes a hyper-localized approach in each market to bring the most relevant online shopping experience for brands, sellers, and shoppers.&#160;</p><p>By understanding each market and its user behaviors means Shopee is able to respond to their needs. As well as having local offices and teams in each of the markets it operates, each market is highly localized in its product categories and marketing campaigns. For example, in Indonesia Shopee launched Shopee Barokah to meet the needs of Muslim users for a variety of Shariah-compliant products and services<strong>, </strong>particularly during the fasting month.&#160;</p><p>Shopee also runs&#160; localized initiatives around festivals such as Chinese New Year or Tet, and at the operational level it offers seven different versions of the app and has a variety of payment options to match specific country-level needs.</p><h2><strong>For customers: more than just shopping</strong></h2><p>One important area of innovation for Shopee is its ability to provide a personalized and social experience for its users.&#160;</p><p>In terms of personalization, Shopee leverages data and AI to identify patterns and insights from users' browsing and purchase data and uses new technologies like AI and AR-powered tools to help brands give their audiences distinct shopping experiences. Instead of focusing solely on driving transactions and competing on price, brands and sellers can win by engaging customers and creating brand affinity through these experiences.&#160;</p><p>Shopee has from the beginning integrated shopping and social. The platform creates immersive experiences by building a strong community that enables users to connect and interact with one another.&#160;</p><p>Features include: Shopee Live (a live streaming feature); Shopee Games (an in-app gaming function); Shopee Feed (an in-app social feed allows users to share content on what they are listing, buying, and selling with the larger Shopee community); and Shopee Live Chat (a chat function that allows buyers to speak with sellers directly and find out more information before and after making a purchase).&#160;</p><p>The company is also using data and AI to make online shopping more secure. For example, scripted machine learning is used to detect potential fraud cases and counterfeit products on the platform, offering users greater peace of mind. At the same time, its integrated mobile wallets ShopeePay and AirPay offer users a convenient and secure option, and in turn helps businesses capture new opportunities.</p><h2><strong>Support for merchants and digital inclusion</strong></h2><p>Shopee is committed to strengthening its partner merchant ecosystem. At the most basic level, the Shopee Seller Centre is continually updated with new functions that make it easier for sellers to track and manage their sales performance, payments, inventories, and deliveries on Shopee:&#160;</p><p>On top of that, in terms of marketing Shopee provides a range of data and visualisation tools to track and obtain shopping insights, as well as a one-stop portal where merchants can create vouchers and other promotional tools. Shopee recently teamed up with Google to launch Google Ads with Shopee, a first-of-its-kind marketing solution for brands to drive sales online. Brands on Shopee will get access to specialized marketing tools to boost their online presence, create deeper engagements with customers, and flexibly manage and measure their marketing campaigns.&#160;</p><p>Shopee is also aiming to power the next wave of digital growth in the region and ensure that more businesses can digitize and tap into the growing opportunity in the region, particularly following the COVID-19 downturn. Support offered includes the Seller Support Package launched in April to help businesses digitize and recover from the pandemic, and&#160; Shopee University, which equips sellers with the knowledge to start their online business. Shopee also offers Seller Masterclasses, which drive sellers to adopt new tools and leverage new trends. One of the specific objectives of the Masterclass is to help sellers better leverage the benefits of live streaming.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
